Commentary

Review of World Economic Trends in the Past Year (Part 1) - Tong 12

Let us examine the course of world economy in the past year. In a word, it can be described as entering a period of extreme decline. Since the breakdown of the World Economic Conference, the economic policies of various countries have diverged and followed extreme paths. Countries have successively adopted economic blockade policies, making this policy the darling of the times. Thus, tariff wars and boycotts of goods have been implemented to benefit domestic industries and exclude the intrusion of foreign economic forces. Since then, the organization of economic blockades has become increasingly strict. For example, the United Kingdom convened representatives from its colonies that attended the World Economic Conference to hold an Imperial Conference and reaffirm the Ottawa Agreement, which shows its efforts in economic blockade. The Netherlands also abandoned its free trade policy and placed the Dutch East Indies under the control of its national economy. The United States also contacted and cooperated with South American countries to conclude new commercial treaties. These are all obvious examples. As for its impact on the domestic aspects of various countries, it can be said that (1) it has activated the industrial sector. Since the breakdown of the World Economic Conference, various countries have continued to implement policies that they believe are most suitable for the actual national economy, supplemented by low-interest monetary policies to create price inflation, making the industrial sector tend to be active. For example, the production volume of the basic steel industry in various countries has increased. This is one example. (2) There has been price inflation. The state of price fluctuations varies slightly from country to country. In countries with a gold standard monetary system, it is weaker. In countries that have abandoned it, it is stronger. In terms of the overall world trend, it has been trending towards significant inflation in the second half of 1933. It has not changed in 1934. Price inflation is nothing more than a prosperity policy of expanding finance and disposing of accumulated goods, indirectly helping to increase the purchasing power of agricultural countries and farmers in general. Therefore, the basis for reflecting the increase in purchasing power can be said to be political rather than economic. Let us consider the situation of the major countries in the world.

On the agricultural country side, the extreme exhaustion caused by the economic downturn suffered by farmers in general was at its peak in the second half of 1933. Since then, it has gradually eased with price inflation. In the United States, from the beginning of the financial panic in 1929 to December 1932, the price of agricultural products fell by 60%. Although the government urgently implemented its active agricultural relief policy through the New Deal, it was still around 20%. The prices of agricultural products, especially cereals, are not easy to raise to the level of general prices for political reasons. Looking at the American agricultural relief movement, the degree of active efforts has been clearly shown to us. However, the effect achieved is still so small. It is easier to imagine the economic situation of the rural areas of other countries.

Since the general economy of the world has recently shown phenomena of price inflation and industrial activity, then in principle, commodity trade should be expected to develop. However, what the facts tell people is very different. Countries want to achieve the perfection of their economic blockade policies internally, actively promoting production and encouraging exports, while setting up tariff barriers externally to exclude foreign goods. International trade is in a situation where it is only possible to shrink under the heavy economic obstacles. In 1933, international trade saw exports of 12 billion U.S. dollars and imports of 10.8 billion U.S. dollars, a decrease of 5.6% in exports and 22.3% in imports compared to the previous year. Although there are no official statistics available for this year, it is feared that the results will not be very good.

The Sichuan Staff Delegation Departs Gan

After Arriving at Xun, Staff Headquarter Will Move Westward by Steamer and Decide to Reside in Chongqing 13

(Hankou) The staff delegation of the military headquarters, consisting of more than 20 people, led by He Guoguang, passed Xun at noon on the 29th and traveled westward by steamer. They are expected to arrive in Hankou on the 30th. Military and political authorities are preparing a warm welcome. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

(Nanchang) He Guoguang, director of the staff delegation stationed in Sichuan, led the heads of various departments, staff officers, secretaries, and all officers and their families, totaling over a hundred people, away from the province by special train at noon on the 29th. Representatives from all sectors of the provincial capital and mass organizations reached over 4,000 to see them off. Xiong Shihui, party and government members, and all officers of the military headquarters crossed the river to bid farewell. Security at the station and wharf was very tight. Before departing, He told the Central News Agency reporter that he and Liu Fucheng were classmates in Sichuan in their youth and colleagues for eight years, with a solid friendship. This time, he was ordered by the chairman to enter Sichuan, and is responsible for assisting in commanding and supervising the suppression of bandits in Sichuan Province. The staff headquarters has decided to reside in Chongqing. Personnel in each department of the delegation, except for political training personnel who have not yet been assigned, have all been appointed and departed today. There is also a group of personnel who were transferred from the military headquarters, and are scheduled to leave Beijing today to assemble in Hankou. They will stay in Hankou for one or two days, and then all enter Sichuan. The political training director of the delegation, Kang Ze, also went to Xun by the same train to transfer students from the political training class. He will enter Sichuan after the organization is in place. The political training personnel of each army and division stationed in Sichuan will be appointed by that department. (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 29th)

(Nanchang) The full title of the staff delegation is the Staff Delegation of the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government. Its organization includes one lieutenant general as director, one major general or lieutenant general as deputy director, ten major general or lieutenant general senior staff officers, an unspecified number of counselors, two colonel secretaries, and one lieutenant colonel. There are also inspectors, adjutants, and telecommunications officers of various ranks. The first department is responsible for military affairs, with one major general as department head, one colonel as deputy department head, and nine staff officers. The second department is responsible for politics, except that the staff officers are changed to department members, the rest is the same as the first department. The general affairs department is headed by a colonel, with more than ten military supply officers and adjutants. The political training department will be determined separately. Political training sub-departments are established in each army and division in Sichuan, totaling 79 officers (excluding the political training department). (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 29th)

(Nanjing) He Guoguang, head of the military headquarters staff delegation, and others, traveled westward from Xun to Hankou on the 29th. The remaining personnel will charter four steamers from Chongqing to welcome them to Sichuan. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

(Nanchang) The senior personnel of the staff delegation who departed with He on the 29th included: Liu Yiren, head of the first department; Xiao Lin, deputy head; Bai Liang, head of the general affairs department; Wang Lantian, director of the medical office; senior staff officers Li Bohua, Tian Xiangfan, Fan Shihong, and Nie Tao; secretary Xia Shilin; and Kang Ze, director of the political training department, who went to Xingzi County by the same train to transfer personnel to Sichuan. Yang Jihui, the deputy director of the delegation, was originally the head of the second department in Sichuan. Wang Youyong is currently still in Shanghai. Li Weilun, the deputy director, left the province earlier on the 28th. (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 29th)

(Chengdu) The bandit suppression headquarters received a telegram from He Guoguang, director of the staff delegation of the military headquarters, stating that the staff delegation personnel would travel westward from Xun to Hankou on the 29th. The headquarters telegraphed Chongqing to charter steamers to welcome them to Sichuan. (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 29th)

Sun Ke Heads North from Beijing 14

(Nanjing) Sun Ke arrived in Beijing from Shanghai on the morning of the 29th, crossed the river at 7 p.m., went to Pukou and took the Pingpu train to Ping to visit his wife, Chen Shuzi, and to inspect the situation in various places and meet with Huang Fu, chairman of the Beiping Political Council, etc. He is scheduled to return to Beijing with his wife in a week. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

The Hebei Provincial Government Strictly Prevents the Remnants of Liu's Bandits from Fleeing into the War Zone

[P Telegram Instructs Four Counties' Militia to Suppress Bandits in Mentougou Area, No Trace of Bandits Found]

(Tianjin) The bandit gang under Liu Guitang was pursued by the newly formed special police force from Fangshan on the afternoon of the 28th and fled towards Tongxian. That night, they encountered the Tongxian Security Regiment in the Xiaohongmen Yongledian area and a fierce battle broke out. The entire city of Tongxian was on alert overnight. On the morning of the 29th, the special police force pursued them, and the bandits fled towards Pinggu County. The provincial government, fearing that the bandit gang would flee into the war zone and join forces with the bandits in Yutian, specially telegraphed the militia of Pinggu, Sanhe, Tongxian, and Bindi counties to cooperate in preventing them. It is reported that the bandit gang, fearing pursuit by government troops, released all the kidnapped hostages along the way to move more quickly. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

(Beiping) After Liu Guitang's remnants fled to Mentougou yesterday, about 200 people were found in the Mayu Village Dahuitang area. The 53rd Army of Wan Fulin's forces immediately sent a Tang regiment to suppress them. The bandits fled as soon as they saw the troops arriving. Until dusk, the Tang regiment continued to search the northwest area of Dahuitang. There were small contacts wherever the unit went, and as a result, the bandits were defeated and fled in a panic towards Zhaizhang. As of this afternoon, there was no trace of bandits in the Mentougou and Shijingshan areas. In addition to dispatching two more regiments to protect the electric light company and power plant in Shijingshan, the 53rd Army is now stationed with mounted infantry teams in Dahuitang, Mayu Village, Mentougou, and other places to strictly prevent the bandits from returning. The Beiping Municipal Public Security Bureau has ordered Lin Yanbin, the director of the Western Suburbs Office, to lead the police and security teams to conduct strict defenses in the Xiangshan Sanjiadian area. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

(Beiping) More than 200 remnant bandits of Liu Guitang suddenly appeared in Shimen, southwest corner of Tongxian, the banner marked as the "Number One Regiment in the World". After the authorities were informed, Shang Zhen, commander of the 32nd Army, immediately dispatched a regiment from the troops stationed in Tongxian to suppress them. Another regiment was transferred from Nanyuan to Tongxian for security. Yin Rugeng said this morning that the Liu bandits' harassment near Tongxian has been surrounded and suppressed by the garrison troops and can be easily resolved. More than 100 bandits were found in Yingshang Village, west of Fangshan County, last month. They burned, killed, looted, and committed all kinds of evils. Fortunately, they were surrounded and dispersed by the Fangshan and Laishui County Security Regiments. Unexpectedly, the bandits gathered together and suddenly reappeared when the county police and security regiments were unprepared. They passed through villages, looting as if in an uninhabited area. The regimental police are contacting neighboring villages' police forces to actively fight back. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

Sichuan Fellow Townsmen Gather to Discuss Methods to Consolidate Sichuan and Pacify Guizhou 15

(Nanjing) Dozens of Sichuan fellow townsmen in Beijing, including Lv Chao, Shi Qingyang, and Zeng Kuangqing, gathered at a residence at noon on the 29th to discuss ways to consolidate Sichuan and pacify Guizhou, due to the intention of the fleeing Communist bandits in Guizhou to enter Sichuan. They jointly telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Central Government, requesting that a large army be dispatched immediately to enter Sichuan to intercept and suppress them. The telegram has been sent. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

(Nanjing) Dozens of Sichuan fellow townsmen, including Lv Hanqun, Shi Qingyang, and Zeng Kuangqing, gathered in Beijing at noon on the 29th to discuss ways to consolidate Sichuan and pacify Guizhou, due to the intention of the fleeing remnant bandits in Guizhou to enter Sichuan. They also jointly telegraphed the Central Government and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, requesting that a large army be dispatched immediately to enter Sichuan to intercept and suppress them, in order to eliminate them as soon as possible. It is reported that the telegram was sent on the 29th. (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 29th)

(Nanjing) Guizhou fellow townsmen in Beijing made three requests to the central government agencies and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek regarding the remnant bandits fleeing to Guizhou: (1) Quickly transfer a large army to Guizhou to suppress the bandits; (2) Clearly order the exemption of Guizhou salt tax surcharges; (3) Improve Guizhou's administration and strictly punish corruption. They also united with fellow townsmen in Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Beiping to make the same requests. (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 29th)

The Issue of Additional Tax on Foreign Rice in the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty 17

There Are Compensatory Methods in Negotiation

(Nanjing) In the Sino-French Vietnamese commercial treaty, regarding the issue of foreign rice tax, the Guangdong local authorities levy local taxes in addition to import duties. Our side said that it is collected from direct consumers and does not seem to be related to the seller. The French side still said that it is harmful to Vietnamese rice sales. When the French ambassador went to Guangdong last time, he exchanged views with the local authorities there. The French ambassador also discussed this with Finance Minister Kong in Shanghai a few days ago. The government believes that there are now compensatory methods in negotiation regarding the issue of Guangdong's additional foreign rice tax, and the French side should be understanding. In this way, the Vietnamese treaty should be resolved soon. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

Explosion at Beipiao Coal Mine 24

53 Chinese Workers Killed

(Tianjin) The Beipiao Coal Mine in Rehe was forcibly occupied by the Japanese after the September 18th Incident, and the mining method was changed, following the model of the Fushun Mine. The manager is a Japanese named Toyoshima Saburo. All the important employees of the mine are Japanese. On the 25th, the fourth roadway of the mine suddenly emitted heavy sulfur and dense smoke. The Japanese engineers and supervisors were unable to rescue them, and it exploded at 4 p.m., penetrating the second roadway into a hole, killing two Japanese engineers and 53 Chinese workers, injuring 37, and causing losses of more than 100,000. The equipment in the second and fourth roadways was destroyed. The fire was very strong on the morning of the 26th. All the mine work was completely stopped, and there is no hope of repairing it in the short term. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

Hebei Province's Second Phase of Extortionate Taxes Cannot Be Cut Completely by the End of the Year 25

(Tianjin) Regarding the abolition of the second phase of extortionate taxes in Hebei Province, only a few counties have filled out and submitted the forms as of now, and they have not yet been actually abolished. The Department of Finance has repeatedly urged the counties, which have all prevaricated due to difficulties. It is no longer possible to complete the abolition by the end of the year in accordance with the departmental orders. The Department of Finance telegraphed the ministry to request an extension of three months. (Special Dispatch on the 29th)

The Yellow River's Ice Floes Arrived Suddenly 26

(Tianjin) The Yellow River's ice floes arrived suddenly. The River Affairs Bureau telegraphed the Department of Construction on the 28th, urgently requesting the allocation of disaster relief funds to gather workers and purchase materials to protect the embankment. The Department of Construction, according to the telegram, has sent a letter to the Department of Finance to expedite the disbursement. (Central News Agency Dispatch on the 29th)

Page 7

Japan Officially Declares the Destruction of the Naval Treaty, Breaking the Balance of Power in the Pacific

The Treaty Remains in Effect for Two Years, The United States' Original Intention to Maintain Peace Remains, Still Cherishing the Hope of Concluding a New Treaty 27

(Tokyo) According to responsible sources, Saito, the Japanese ambassador to the United States, following the instructions of his government, will submit the notification of Japan's abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty to US Secretary of State Hull at 12:00 on Saturday (Washington time). (Reuters Dispatch on the 29th)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota telegraphed the Japanese ambassadors to England, France, and Italy, instructing them to notify the governments of their respective countries of Japan's abandonment of the Washington Treaty and to strongly argue Japan's disarmament policy. (Japanese Allied Press Dispatch on the 29th)

(Washington) Japan today formally abandoned the naval limitation treaty. The Japanese Ambassador to the United States, Saito, today handed over the order from Tokyo to abandon the treaty to the State Department. The full text is one hundred words long. Saito visited Secretary of State Hull this afternoon in accordance with diplomatic practice and handed over the Tokyo instructions in person. The Japanese Embassy also released this statement to the press at the same time. This statement is nothing more than a restatement of Saito's previous verbal expressions to Hull. The US government did not express surprise at this, but the official impression given by the statement is very deep. The fourteen-year balance of power in the Pacific created by the self-concluded agreement of the three countries may be washed away by this. But the government hopes to conclude a new treaty. If this is hopeless, observers have expressed that politicians and diplomats can use their remarks to maintain peace in the Far East. Japan indicated in its note that after 1936, Japan does not want to be restricted by the naval ratio of 5:5:3. This alone is enough to show the spirit of challenging the treaty. Officials claim that whether there will be a naval arms race in 1936 will depend on whether Japan will engage in building warships after the naval treaty expires. Officials secretly expressed great disappointment, but on the surface, they declared that the US policy is to stabilize the public opinion of major countries, so they will avoid any provocative statements or actions to weaken the possibility of concluding a new treaty after the expiration of the naval treaty. It is said that Japan's declaration of abolishing the treaty will increase discussions related to opening up naval and army bases in the Pacific, but the government denies this discussion. It is learned that naval officers generally believe that although Japan has abandoned the naval treaty, the United States will still maintain a peaceful attitude and will continue to work to obtain an understanding in 1935. Most Japanese newspapers declare that the main issue in 1935 will be related to the coordination between Italy and France. (National Telegram on the 28th)

Japan's Notice of Abolition 28

(Tokyo) Ambassador Saito to the United States, following the government's order, met with US Secretary of State Hull at noon on the 29th (2 a.m. on the 30th Japan time) and formally handed over the Japanese government's notice of abolishing the Washington Treaty as follows:

Dear Sir, I am honored to inform you on behalf of my government as follows. The Government of Japan, in accordance with Article 23 of the Treaty relating to the Limitation of Naval Armament signed in Washington on February 6, 1922, hereby notifies the Government of the United States of its intention to renounce the said Treaty, and therefore the said Treaty shall cease to have effect after December 31, 1936. Saito. (Japanese Allied Press Dispatch on the 29th)

Aims of Tokyo's Statement 29

(Tokyo) The Japanese government issued a statement on the aims of abolishing the Washington Treaty on the afternoon of the 29th as follows: During the preparatory negotiations for naval disarmament, the Japanese government cooperated with the countries concerned to consolidate Japan's national defense and to fully exert the achievements of disarmament, so as to establish a fair and appropriate new agreement, and thereby avoid the threat of aggression between major naval powers, and at the same time hope to reduce the burden on the people as much as possible. Based on this view, the Japanese government, as a result of careful consideration of the root points that can be used as a new disarmament agreement, has decided on the following points:

(1) The existing naval treaty is considered to be formed in a way that the military strength between major naval powers is unequal. Referring to the current situation of the progress of ships, weapons, aircraft, etc., it is learned that the above-mentioned method is extremely difficult to ensure the consolidation of Japan's national defense in the future. Therefore, in the new disarmament agreement, the above-mentioned ratioism should be replaced with the common maximum limit of the military strength that each country can possess, so that it can be used as a method of agreement.

(2) (A) In order to give play to the spirit of military reduction, the above-mentioned limit must be reduced as much as possible. (B) At the same time, in order to make it difficult for countries to attack and easy to defend, the military power of attack should be completely abolished or reduced as much as possible, and the military power of defense should be prepared. Following the above-mentioned main points, to draw up a new treaty is most in line with the original intention of military reduction, and can thereby ensure the permanent consolidation of national defense of various countries. This is Japan's fundamental position, and it is also expressed to the countries concerned. However, the Washington Naval Limitation Treaty not only recognizes the types of ships dedicated to attack, which the Japanese government intends to completely abolish, as being retained, but also stipulates the inequality of military strength between major naval powers by ratioism. Therefore, the continuation of the treaty is indeed impossible for the Japanese government to accept in accordance with the fundamental policy. The inferior ratio being regulated by it is even more damaging to the self-esteem of the Japanese people, so it has never given satisfaction to the people forever. Therefore, the Japanese government now awaits the end of the treaty in Showa 11, that is, the initial validity period stipulated in the treaty has now been reached, and at the same time considers it an appropriate time to abolish it. In accordance with the provisions of the treaty, it is necessary to exercise the notification of abolition by the end of this year. The above-mentioned intentions of the Japanese government have already been notified to the British and American sides in advance. However, because the Japanese side hopes that this preparatory negotiation will make every effort to be effective and make a plan to generate results, it is intended to cooperate sincerely with the countries concerned to exercise the notification of abolition, and then cooperate to promote the establishment of a new treaty, which can be considered appropriate. Therefore, the Japanese government has explained the above-mentioned reasons to all the countries concerned and advised them to jointly notify the abolition of the treaty, but all countries have not agreed. Now, the Japanese government has decided to notify the US government in writing of its intention to abolish the Washington Naval Treaty alone, in accordance with the provisions of Article 23 of the treaty. This is its origin. Since the above-mentioned notice of abolition has been clearly stipulated in the treaty, the rights of all contracting countries in the treaty are already obvious. Self-evident, the Japanese government's measures this time regarding the abolition of the Washington Treaty are to expect to establish a new treaty that is the most fair and appropriate and the most in line with the spirit of disarmament, and this is the inevitable conclusion of the above-mentioned Japanese side in accordance with the fundamental policy. Even after the Japanese government has notified the abolition of the treaty, it is still prepared to make friendly consultations with the countries concerned, in order to establish a new agreement that is fair and reasonable. This is a heartfelt hope that never ends. As for intentions such as promoting military expansion or harming international peace, it is not within Japan's dreams. The fact that Japan is demanding the complete abolition or a great reduction in ships of attack, in order to establish the principle of non-threatening and non-aggression, should have revealed its intention. If the countries concerned are humble and frank, and think carefully about this point, they will be able to understand the appropriateness of the Japanese proposal. Therefore, if the countries can agree to completely abolish the attacking ships, or because the existing forces are greatly reduced due to the large reduction, and at the same time the common maximum limit of the military strength they possess can be agreed, then the countries will not be threatened by any country, and ensure their sense of security. Only then can a permanent peaceful relationship be established. This is what the Japanese government believes. (Japanese Allied Press Dispatch on the 29th)

Great Britain Expresses Deep Regret 30

(London) All sectors of the British people deeply regret Japan's abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty. The biggest step towards military reduction has become a pie in the sky. Public opinion is that Japan has the inherent right to abolish the treaty, but Britain has made great contributions to the treaty, saving the signatory countries a great deal of naval expenditure. This move by Japan will not only affect naval disarmament, but also general disarmament. However, Britain still intends to continue to make the greatest possible efforts to complete an agreement to replace the Washington Treaty. (Reuters Dispatch on the 29th)

(London) Although Londoners deeply regret Japan's abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty, Reuters learned that Britain does not regard this as a tendency to break the entire collective peace system. Japan's willingness to abolish the other two important treaties that are the same as the Washington Treaty organization, namely the Nine-Power Treaty and the Four-Power Treaty, does not indicate that the Pacific belongs to Japan. However, Japan's abolition of one of these three treaties will make political disputes more likely to be raised when naval talks are reopened in the future. (Reuters)

France's Position Is Different 31

(London) As for France, it is heard that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is not anxious about Japan's move, because France has expressed dissatisfaction with many points of the treaty since the day it was signed. According to news from diplomatic visitors, the main reason why the French government does not agree with Japan's abolition of the Washington Treaty is that France is unwilling to advocate the termination of any treaty for world peace. France now seems to be putting forward its own specific suggestions, which are naturally related to its position on Italy. France does not seem to be satisfied with absolute equality with Italy. (Reuters Dispatch on the 29th)

US Representative Left England Yesterday 32

Tokyo's Instructions Reject the British Plan, The Atmosphere for Reopening Negotiations Is Getting Darker

(London) The atmosphere for the resumption of the London naval talks is now getting darker day by day. The US representative is scheduled to return to the United States tonight. The US side has recently expressed its intention in earnest. If the Japanese side does not actively change its views today and make future discussions have a more hopeful basis, then the US representative does not want to come to the talks again or participate in the naval conference. Now the US representative has returned home, and the impression he has is that the Japanese side's views have not changed from beginning to end. Then, will the Japanese view change after all? It will be decided by the results of the negotiations between Britain and Japan. Although the Japanese representative Yamamoto has not yet received instructions to return home, he may not stay in London for long. US representative Standley hosted a banquet for Japanese representative Yamamoto yesterday. After the meal, he talked with Yamamoto alone for half an hour. Yamamoto showed him the instructions from Tokyo that he received this week, and it is heard that this instruction is a rejection. Yamamoto then met with Chappell, a naval officer of the British Navy Department. In the evening, Cregie of the British Foreign Office went to see US representative Davis to see him off and told him that the United Kingdom will continue to negotiate with Tokyo through diplomatic channels, hoping to establish a basis for future discussions. When Davis heard this, he wished him success. The US representative boarded the ship and left England at 8:30 tonight. The US representative believes that the naval conference may not be held before 1936. If there is no real hope of concluding a treaty in the current situation, it is useless to hold the meeting. Reuters has learned that the US side believes that Tokyo's recent instructions have given a definite rejection to the British compromise plan to have all parties declare their warship building procedures. (Reuters Dispatch on the 29th)

International Espionage on the Eve of World War 33

(Special Dispatch from Shenyang) Due to the breakdown of the recent naval disarmament conference, the Japanese puppet regime is frantically preparing for war, actively provoking the Soviet Union. Military disputes frequently occur along the Soviet-"Manchukuo" border. The prelude to a world war has manifested in the intensified international espionage war. Japanese spies have been discovered in British Singapore and the American Samoa, among other places. An attaché at the Japanese embassy in Tokyo, named Takemiya, used a woman to gather military intelligence. British and American journalists stationed in Yokohama have been arrested on suspicion of espionage. However, the most active area for espionage is undoubtedly the Northeast. In Shenyang alone, there are over thirty foreign-affiliated intelligence agencies. In Hunchun, along the Russian-"Manchukuo" border, Andong, along the "Manchukuo"-Korean border, and Dalian port, several people are searched and detained daily on suspicion of espionage. Such phenomena are not uncommon; they are inevitable on the eve of a world war.

Moscow Newspaper Discusses Recent World Situation 34

Deepening Contradictions of Imperialism - Pacific War Imminent

(Moscow) Pravda published an article on the recent world situation entitled "Preparations for War in the Pacific," stating, "The failure of the Washington Naval Treaty was predetermined by the development of imperialist contradictions, and the treaty's conclusion was itself a result of these contradictions. In the past fourteen years, the balance of power among imperialist nations has fundamentally changed. Since the rise of German fascism, the threat of future war has permeated Europe. Simultaneously, Anglo-American conflicts have intensified. Japanese imperialism is seizing this opportunity to establish its dominance in the Western Pacific. War in the Pacific is now more imminent than ever. The nations that will participate in this war do not misunderstand its widespread nature." The newspaper firmly believes that the fate of future naval conferences is already in serious doubt. (TASS dispatch, 28th)

Philippine Independence Issue 35

Current Situation is Dangerous

(New York) Recently, many American newspapers have argued that, given the current general situation in the Pacific, the Philippines should become an American dominion to avoid the dangers of complete independence. The American Senate investigation team currently in the Philippines seems to hold the same view. As for Philippine Senate President Quezon, while he supports adopting a dominion system, he requests that the United States not sever trade relations with the Philippines as stipulated in the Philippine Independence Act (i.e., taxing goods imported from the Philippines into the United States on the same basis as foreign goods) and that close economic ties with the Philippines be allowed. The American Senate investigation team's response to this Philippine hope has been evasive, likely because powerful American economic circles oppose it. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

(Special Dispatch from Hong Kong) Philippine Senate President Quezon, on his way back to the Philippines from the United States via Hong Kong, told people, "Even if the United States withdraws from the Philippines, I cannot imagine Japan occupying the island, as feared by the Hearst newspapers. The United States has already proposed Philippine independence; we can only accept it. We will not change our determination."

Japan Expands Commercial Policy, Adopts More Active Diplomacy Toward China

Simultaneous Political and Economic Efforts, Compromise with Britain to End Confrontation 36

(Tokyo) Although Japan's international trade is suppressed by various countries, it still maintains its strength. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has decided on the following trade promotion policies to cope with the upcoming extraordinary international situation:

Securing Existing Markets 37

(A) The British industrial inspection delegation's examination of the Far East will lead to the establishment of an Anglo-Japanese Trade Commission. Japan expects its activities to cease the state of Anglo-Japanese commercial confrontation worldwide and to implement mutual concessions and compromises. (B) Awaiting the launch of the Japan-"Manchukuo" Economic Cooperation Committee to establish the Japan-Manchukuo economic alliance. (C) Trade promotion policies toward China will be pursued in parallel with political and cultural work toward China, using active measures. Preparations are currently underway. (D) Trade with Southeast Asia, especially with the Netherlands, will be actively adjusted, based on the principle of continuing the Japan-Netherlands trade talks. (E) Trade with the United States and South America, centered on trade with Brazil, will be vigorously advanced by taking advantage of opportunities to dispatch economic and cultural missions. (F) Trade with Russia will be developed opportunistically when over 93 million yuan worth of goods are handed over in connection with the purchase price of the Chinese Eastern Railway.

Coping with Countries with Trade Surpluses 38

Implementing trade adjustment policies toward countries with trade surpluses with Japan, such as the United States, Australia, Germany, Canada, Norway, and Sweden. (A) Negotiations for the conclusion of a new Japan-Australia trade treaty are progressing between the Australian Federal Government and Consul-General Murai. (B) Trade adjustment negotiations on imports and exports between Canadian Minister to Japan and Foreign Minister Hirota have already begun. (C) Efforts to reduce tariffs requested by the Norwegian government are currently underway and are expected to be successful soon. These are the fundamental principles of Japan's economic diplomacy for the coming year: (1) securing existing markets, (2) acquiring new markets, and (3) coping with countries with trade surpluses. (Jiji dispatch, 29th)

(Tokyo) From an economic diplomacy perspective, this year will end with a passive attitude. From next year, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs plans to change to proactive diplomacy and has already made the following preparations:

(1) Relations with China 39

Starting in April next year, a survey of China's economic situation is planned. In addition to the Commercial Counselor Yokotake stationed in Shanghai, personnel will also be dispatched from the Ministry.

(1) Netherlands-Japan Talks 40

Awaiting Representative Nagaoka's return to the country in January to hold six province conferences and negotiate methods for the second stage.

(1) Relations with Britain 41

Concrete coordination will be carried out based on the report of the Pumphrey industrial inspection delegation.

(1) Relations with the United States 42

In parallel with the Anglo-Japanese Trade Cooperation Council, civil mediation such as the Japan-US Trade Cooperation Council will cooperate with each other to generate new opportunities for international coordination. (Dentsu dispatch, 29th)

A Key to Central European Peace, New Progress in Italian-French Negotiations

Both Countries' Difficulties in Principle Are Reached Compromise, Laval's Rome Trip Not Far Off, Guaranteeing Austria's Independence by Six-Nation Treaty 47

(Paris) Whether Foreign Minister Laval will go to Rome is still unknown, but newspapers here all say that French-Italian negotiations have made satisfactory progress, and that the Foreign Minister may visit Rome in early January. Some newspapers even mentioned the Italian reception procedures. Le Petit Parisien reported: "The current French-Italian negotiations aim to ensure the security of Central Europe and the independence of Austria. This is what the world expects, and smooth progress is expected soon. After consulting with the Little Entente countries and the Austrian government yesterday evening, the French Foreign Ministry sent an important document to the Italian government through the French ambassador to Italy. Therefore, well-informed sources believe that tomorrow or even today will be an important date for a decision."

L'Echo de Paris reported that the document sent by the French Foreign Ministry to the Italian government proposed that the neighboring countries of Austria, namely Italy, Germany, Hungary, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia, conclude a protocol guaranteeing the independence of Austria. If Germany and Hungary raise reservations among these five countries, then Italy, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia should first sign the protocol, and Germany and Hungary can join later when they express their agreement. This is the first step. The second step, which requires Mussolini's support, is roughly as follows: Countries signing the protocol guaranteeing Austria's independence should also guarantee each other's security if their borders are adjacent. Thus, Italy and Yugoslavia must guarantee each other's security. By analogy, the Central European Security Pact can be extended to Central and Eastern Europe, and the Northeast European Security Pact can be linked to the Balkan Pact, forming a security network covering the entire European continent. In addition, L'Echo de Paris also learned that Czech Foreign Minister Beneš and Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu seem to have accepted this French proposal, which is considered extremely gratifying, as people are deeply concerned that Laval may have neglected the Little Entente countries. Now that Beneš and Titulescu have accepted, this concern can be dispelled. In short, given the current situation between Italy and the Little Entente countries, France can approach Italy on the one hand without alienating its allies on the other. (Havas dispatch, 29th)

(Paris) The tense situation between France and Italy now shows signs of ending. Although the date of French Foreign Minister Laval's visit to Rome has not yet been set, it appears to be not far off. Le Journal de Paris even said that Laval will leave on January 2, indicating that French-Italian contact has made good progress. The French Foreign Minister's visit to Rome indicates that the most difficult issues between the two countries have been resolved, at least in principle. Yesterday, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini met with the French ambassador to Italy. It is said that the French ambassador then informed the Italian Prime Minister of Laval's latest proposal. The purpose of French policy is not only to seek peace in Austria but also to seek security in the Danube region, so that the dispute between Italy and the Little Entente countries over the Austrian issue can be resolved. According to reliable sources, a draft treaty guaranteeing Austria's independence will soon be signed in Rome by Italy, Yugoslavia, Czechoslovakia, Germany, and Hungary. The above-mentioned countries are all Austria's neighbors on the ground. If Germany and Hungary wish to temporarily reserve their attitude, other countries will sign immediately and allow Germany and Hungary to join later. Although France and Romania do not border Austria, they will also be invited to participate in this treaty. The signatory countries will guarantee the integrity of their borders to each other. The most serious obstacle to this plan is whether Hungary will abandon its policy of revising the treaty, and whether Italy can accept a plan that stabilizes the existing borders. Current negotiations focus on the European situation, but the cession of African land has also been discussed. However, the land that France will cede is a strip of land in the southern part of Libya and a part of the northern part of French Somaliland. This plan also stipulates reciprocal tariff and commodity quota measures. (Reuters dispatch, 29th)

League of Nations Performance Report for 1934

The Accession of Soviet Russia and Other Countries is Somewhat Satisfactory, Technical Cooperation with China is Good, The Resolution of the Hungarian-Yugoslav Dispute is Commendable 52

(Geneva) The Secretariat of the League of Nations has recently completed and published a report on the achievements of the League of Nations over the past year, expressing hope for the future without being overly optimistic. The report stated that 1933 was a difficult year, and 1934 also presented many difficulties, as the disarmament conference had stalled and relations between countries had regressed economically. However, several matters were satisfactory: first, Soviet Russia, Afghanistan, and Ecuador all joined the League of Nations as member states; second, the Saar plebiscite was prepared in a fair and methodical manner; and third, the extremely thorny dispute between Hungary and Yugoslavia was resolved. All of these are commendable. The report concludes that various technical organizations are deeply beneficial to the work of the League of Nations. Therefore, Czech Foreign Minister Beneš, then Chairman of the Executive Council of the League of Nations for this year, said after the completion of the League of Nations' performance report, "Judging from the facts of the year, we are not disappointed with the League of Nations' conclusions. Because there is currently a concrete and positive force and trend in the world that is resisting the forces that could disrupt international political life and preventing them from doing harm. The concrete and positive force and trend that we should first mention is the League of Nations." Among the international political issues in 1934, there was also the South American dispute. The report was pleased that the dispute between Peru and Colombia over Leticia had been resolved. As for the dispute between Paraguay and Bolivia over the Chaco, the League of Nations has been working continuously to resolve it, and the outcome has been that all member states have agreed to ban the shipment of arms to the belligerent countries. The report expressed support for the League of Nations' technical cooperation with China, stating that the League of Nations Intellectual Cooperation Organization has been assisting in the job placement of Chinese intellectuals and technicians. The Chinese government has decided to establish such job placement offices in Nanjing and the West to make it easier for Chinese students studying in Europe and the United States to receive vocational training to meet the current needs of China's economic construction. The League of Nations has also assisted China in carrying out various health and veterinary projects, while the transport and transportation agencies are focusing on highways and water conservancy in cooperation with the National Economic Council of China. The League of Nations also sent Dr. Rajchman to China last year as a technical liaison officer between the League of Nations and China. Dr. Rajchman's term expired in August of this year, and he prepared a report on the technical cooperation between the League of Nations and China in accordance with the resolution of the Executive Council's League of Nations and China Technical Cooperation Committee on March 17 of this year, submitting it to the League of Nations' technical agencies. His report recognized that the cooperation was very good. Regarding the problem of narcotics trafficking, the League of Nations report stated that the 1931 Geneva Convention (restricting the manufacture of narcotics and suppressing their distribution) has been strictly and universally implemented by all parties, so the quantity of legal narcotics trafficking has gradually decreased. The League of Nations is now working to prepare a draft convention to punish the illegal trafficking of narcotics. The League of Nations has been able to lay a foundation for this matter, which is the basis for establishing international conventions, so that all countries in the world can be covered by its scope. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Death of Hague Court President Dr. Adachi 53

Another Loss for Japanese Diplomats

(Amsterdam) Dr. Adachi, who has served as President of the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague since 1931, passed away here today at the age of sixty-five. Dr. Adachi was one of Japan's most famous diplomats and legal scholars, having served as an envoy to Mexico, Belgium, and France, among other countries, and was a key figure in the Japanese delegation to the League of Nations for nine years. After graduating from Tokyo University in 1892, he joined the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The following year, he was transferred to the Japanese Legation in Rome as an attaché, taking the opportunity to study international law. After three years, he was appointed Secretary of the Japanese Legation in Paris, and he had already earned the reputation of an international law expert. After returning to Japan from Europe, he lectured on law and continued to serve in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. In 1912, he was sent as an envoy to Mexico, and in 1917, he was sent to Belgium, and was one of the Japanese representatives at the Paris Peace Conference, and joined the committee to draft the Statute of the Permanent Court of International Justice. In 1921, he served as the Japanese representative to the League of Nations, in 1927 he was sent to France, and in 1931 he served as President of the International Court of Justice, and now he has died in office. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

Foreign Crew Members of Hong Wah Steamer Go on Strike 65

Twelve Ships Cease Operations

(Hong Kong) Foreign crew members of the Hong Wah Steamer went on strike on the evening of the 29th. The Hong Wu and Hong Jiang steamers have both ceased operations. (29th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Chinese Seamen's Union and the Chinese Marine Engineers' Union resolved this afternoon to go on strike at midnight tonight. This action by the two unions is due to the fact that monthly salaries are too low to cover living expenses. Thirteen river steamers will be affected. There are forty British crew members. Initially, someone came forward to mediate, but unexpectedly, Sun Boming (transliteration), a wealthy shipowner in Hong Kong, dismissed four senior crew members of the Yutong (transliteration) ship and replaced them with Norwegians and Germans. As a result, the unrest grew. The two unions are now discussing inviting crew members of other ships with wages recognized by the unions to join the strike. The two unions have also ordered striking crew members to stay on board to protect the owner's property, in fact fearing that crew members who are not members of the unions will take over the ships. The ship owners are attempting to request the Hong Kong government to intervene, but have been refused. (29th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Although mediated by a fair group, the Chinese Seamen's Union still went on strike tonight, affecting forty employees and twelve ships. The owners of nine ships have agreed to pay wages as originally stipulated. The real reason for this strike is that the mail steamer Yueton dismissed four British crew members and hired an unemployed Norwegian shipowner as a replacement. A representative of the Seamen's Union stated that the strike would continue until the four are reinstated. Although other shipowners have agreed to pay wages, this is unrelated to the matter. According to reliable sources, key officers on inland river steamers only receive a monthly salary of 200 yuan, which is lower than the monthly salary of a female typist in Hong Kong. The shipping situation after the strike is extremely poor, and the situation is becoming more chaotic because some crew members are willing to accept wages lower than the standard wage. Some poorly paid crew members are unwilling to protest for fear of losing their jobs. It is heard that some captains and engineers only receive a monthly salary of 170 yuan. (29th National News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic sources, after Mr. and Mrs. Stumm were kidnapped and harmed by bandits, their young daughter was rescued by our military and local authorities. Yutian Disputes Still Being Resolved 101

Bandits Seize the Opportunity to Plunder, Devastating the Area. Security Forces and Local Militias are Irreconcilable. Authorities Decide to Adopt a Radical Solution.

Beiping Correspondence: The Yutian militia conflicts have reignited, devastating the area. Authorities are currently devising a solution to alleviate the people's suffering. Details are as follows:

The conflict between the Yutian militias has both long-term and recent causes. The local security force was originally reorganized from Shi Yousan's old troops. At that time, they were transferred from Qinhuangdao to Yutian as an unavoidable measure under certain circumstances. Shortly after their deployment, they clashed with the local militia. After a month of disputes, Yin Rugeng, the Administrative Commissioner of the Jimi District, went to mediate, and the provincial government reassigned Han Dianbang as the commander of the security force, barely resolving the crisis. However, the resentment between the militias was not fundamentally resolved. After Han Dianbang took office, the force and the militias did not get along, eventually causing trouble and driving Han away. As a result, the security force and the militia became enemies again. The security force has over 2,000 men, and Wang Bingxiao's militia also has over 1,000 men. The bases of both sides are close to each other. Every day at 5:00 p.m., they deploy teams to patrol as if facing a major enemy, watching each other's movements. This has been going on for more than a day. Recently, a part of the security force attempted to seize the militia's weapons. At the same time, Feng Peng, an officer of the security force, was attacked by the militia at Yaming Bridge. As a result, the conflict reignited. Zhu Shiqin, a standing member of the War Zone Clearance Committee, went to mediate. Although the conflict between the two sides has temporarily stopped, they still confront each other. During this period, bandits in the county seized the opportunity to plunder, burning and killing everywhere, causing chaos throughout the county. Tangjiazhuang and other villages were burned and looted completely, devastating the area and causing significant losses. According to people from Yutian, the residents of the surrounding villages are now suffering from bandit disturbances, living in dire straits, while the residents within the area are startled several times a night. Only three or four shops are barely managing to stay open, while the rest have closed. The losses in the county this time are extremely heavy, and it will take at least three to five years to restore the area to its original state.

Seeing the devastation of the area, the authorities are seeking a solution and plan to use a radical approach: transferring the security force in the area to Qinhuangdao and sending a new security force to take over their defense. The militia will then be reorganized. Zhu Shile is coordinating with all parties. The security force has agreed to be transferred from Yutian, but has set the disbandment of the militia as a condition. The authorities are determined to handle this matter impartially and resolve it thoroughly to avoid future troubles. Zhu Shiqin traveled to Tianjin, Tangshan and other places to negotiate. He returned to Beiping via Tianjin the night before and went to visit Huang Fu at the Political Consolidation Committee yesterday morning for instructions. At 1:00 p.m., he went to Tianjin again to negotiate. The future is still difficult to predict. However, the authorities are quite determined this time and will not handle it as perfunctorily as they did last time, in order to fundamentally resolve the problem once and for all. (December 27th)

Gold and Silver 102

British Gold: This morning, the price of gold in London was 140 shillings, 11 and a half pence, up one penny.

British Silver: The price of silver in London today for spot was 24 and five-sixteenths pence, and for futures 24 and seven-eighths pence, both up one-eighth pence.

American Silver: The Canadian silver market opened today, jumping 65 pounds sterling, due to the rise in the London silver market.

Exchange Rates 103

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was sluggish this morning. The opening exchange rate for British pounds to U.S. dollars was 4 dollars, 43 and five-sixteenths cents, lower by one-eighth cent than the closing exchange rate of British pounds to U.S. dollars yesterday. This price remained unchanged until closing.

British-French: The British-French exchange market was sluggish today. The opening price was 74 francs, 71 centimes, the same as the closing price yesterday. It was stable in the morning, and fell 6 pounds sterling to 74 francs, 65 centimes at closing.

Cotton and Wheat 104

American Cotton: The cotton market opened, up about two pounds sterling, then stabilized.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market closed unchanged today. The May futures price remained at 6.83.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market's May futures closed today at 5 shillings, two and a half pence, up .75.

American Wheat: The wheat market rose slightly. The Winnipeg price was up .25.

Rubber 105

London: The London rubber market was calm. At noon, the transaction price for April and June futures was 6 and seven-sixteenths pence, unchanged.

New York: The rubber market was also quite active, opening up six pounds sterling. It continued to rise by three or four pounds sterling in the following forty-five minutes.

Securities 106

New York: The transactions in the securities market this morning in the half hour after opening gave the impression that yesterday's surge would continue today. The market situation at the opening was quite active, with prices of various securities rising from fractions to one pound sterling. Industrial stocks remained popular, as positive commercial news led to good demand. Automobile stocks were bought. The talk of inflation circulating on Wall Street this morning seemed to be the reason for the rise in securities prices. Some quarters believe that the new Congress will certainly approve inflation, and the shortage of the budget, the needs of winter relief, and the necessity of borrowing are also being spread by word of mouth. Speculators, seeing this situation, are becoming more active. Hopes from all sides seem to be the same. Tax-avoidance selling seems to have disappeared. Speakers predict that the surge will continue to expand.

Recent News from North China Diplomacy 108

Negotiations on the war zone issue show promise; highway and air routes are still under discussion.

Beijing Correspondence: Recent negotiations in Beijing among representatives from various parties regarding North China diplomacy are showing progress. The long-pending unresolved issues concerning the war zone have also been discussed several times by the responsible personnel of the War Zone Clearance Committee and Ii and Shibayama, etc., and there is some progress. The main points of the discussion are roughly as follows:

(1) The issue of the security forces: The disputes between the two sides on this matter concern the number of personnel and weapons. The Japanese side previously insisted that the total number of personnel should not exceed 5,000, and that no weapons other than guns should be carried. The Chinese side insisted that the number of personnel should be 9,000, and that, in addition to rifles, light and heavy machine guns should be carried. As a result of the current negotiations, the Japanese side has made some concessions: the number of new security forces should not exceed 5,000 in addition to the original security forces in the war zone. Regarding weapons, heavy firearms cannot be carried, but there is still room for negotiation regarding light machine guns. The Japanese side also expressed its willingness to assist in matters such as cracking down on vagrant Japanese and preventing bandits from outside the Great Wall line from invading the war zone.

(2) The dispute over tax checkpoints at various passes of the Great Wall: The Japanese side believes that since both sides have set up checkpoints at various passes to collect taxes, a liaison method should be adopted to avoid disputes. The Chinese side is currently considering this matter. At the same time, tax officials from various passes are meeting in Beijing to discuss everything and submit the agreed-upon methods to the Ministry of Finance for approval.

(3) The issue of taking over Malanyu: In principle, the Japanese side has always acknowledged the takeover, but there are several additional requirements. At the same time, the Japanese puppet troops in the area are using the excuse that the barracks outside the pass have not been completed to refuse to withdraw, which is why it has been difficult to achieve this to this day. Representatives from all parties in Beijing have also discussed this matter. Although the various issues have not been completely resolved, there seems to be some progress compared to before. Ii and Sakei, the chief of staff of the Japanese North China Garrison Headquarters, came to Beijing from Tianjin and had another round of discussions with various parties. Ii has already returned east, while Sakei is still in Beijing. In recent days, the frequent comings and goings of important Japanese figures, in addition to the war zone issue, the highway and air route issues are actually the center of the discussions. The Japanese side attaches great importance to this matter, and the Chinese negotiators are also taking a cautious approach. (26th)

Suzhou 109

Arrest of a Kidnapper in Guangfu Township

The kidnapper Sun Guilin, together with Chen Zhongying and two others, kidnapped Zhu Shunshi, a five-year-old, in Xishan Township during the summer of this year, and took him to Ben Niu. Later, the victim was redeemed by the owner for a price of 1,000 yuan. Sun was arrested by the local public security sub-station in Guangfu Township a few days ago and sent to the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, the Second District of the Water Public Security Bureau brought him back and handed him over to the detective team for interrogation. The bandit has confessed to the kidnapping and extortion.

Songjiang 110

Shanghai Police Bureau's Request to Extradite a Robber Denied

The case of the robbery of the Rihoto Silver Shop in the Japanese Concession early in the morning, and the shooting of the manager Zhao Houzhuang, has caused a stir in the city and countryside. Everyone believes that during the winter defense period, robberies occurring in broad daylight endanger the business of merchants. Fortunately, the Water Patrol Special Forces intercepted the robber Zhao Zhiyi on the same day, and he confessed to the crime without hesitation. A pistol was also found, which belonged to the Shanghai Municipal Police Team. It turns out that the robber Zhao's father, Zhao Fusheng, is currently employed as a detective in the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. He requested an extension of his leave to return to his hometown to bury his mother. His son Zhiyi came to Shanghai to continue his leave and was suggested by Qiu Liangkang to secretly steal his father's pistol and come to Songjiang to commit the robbery. Qiu, who committed the robbery with him, is now at large, and Zhao's father, Zhao Fusheng, has been placed under surveillance for the theft of the pistol. Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau sent personnel to Songjiang to identify the pistol and extradite Zhao Zhiyi to Shanghai for interrogation, but the local county government refused the extradition request because the case was of great importance.

Wuxi 111

Female Silk Factory Workers Petition for Wages

The Xingji Silk Factory under the Iron Tree Bridge outside the South Gate recently suddenly closed down, and the manager, Ji Yunchu, avoided meeting with the workers. More than 3,000 yuan in wages are owed to the workers. After repeated visits to the factory by the female workers to demand payment, they dragged Ji Zenrong, the silk room director, and the car managers Li Dezai, Gu Zhongliang, Feng Chunchu, Qian Shoukui, and Feng Zhuliang into the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau one after another, but to no avail. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday (the 28th), the female workers gathered again, numbering three to four hundred, each holding incense sticks, and dragging Ji Zenrong and Wang Jiepu with them, and marched in formation to the county government to petition. They were stopped by the gatekeepers. The female workers then went to the local branch court, but were also stopped. They then went to the Public Security Bureau, where Inspector Wang received them and interrogated Ji Zenrong. According to Ji, the factory only had 1,360 yuan, which was deposited in the Zhenyuan Silk Factory, and there was no other way. After Inspector Wang's mediation, the female workers' November wages were paid out at an 80% rate from the 1,360 yuan yesterday (the 29th). However, the female workers, because there was still no solution for the rest of the wages, will petition the county party headquarters again. The factory's car manager Qian Shoukui and others also dragged Ji Yunchu's wife Bei, who is the director of the factory's sorting room Xu Junyu, into the Second Branch yesterday and transferred her to the Third Branch to be handled together.

Changzhou 112

Murder for Profit Case in the Sixth District

Wang Quansheng, a farmer from Shihsiang Village in Bantang Township, about two li east of the Sixth District of Wuyi, was about twenty years old and unmarried. He lived alone, farming for a living, and had some savings in his hands. He suddenly disappeared on the fourth day of the old lunar month. It has been nearly twenty days since then, and there has been no news of him. The villagers found a bloodstain in Quansheng's bedroom, and rumors spread that Quansheng had been murdered. It was then discovered that Wang Jinshu and Zhou Heshang from the vicinity had gone to call at the door the night Quansheng disappeared, and Zhou Heshang's behavior was usually improper. Therefore, Quansheng's relatives reported to the Bantang Sixth District Office. The district chief Xie Jun arrested the two suspects, Zhou and Wang. It was also discovered that Wang Chunsheng was also highly suspected, and he was temporarily detained together. While District Chief Xie was investigating, Wang Quan's corpse was suddenly found in the river in Bantang Township. The villagers salvaged the body, and there were indeed serious injuries on his body. District Chief Xie reported the case to the county court on the 28th and requested that personnel be sent to examine the body. The court prosecutor, Guan Junjie, supervised officials and went to the countryside on the 29th to examine the body and brought the suspects to the case for interrogation and handling.

Gaoyou 113

Four Families Robbed in Yigou Township

Yigou Township, 15 li east of the city, is a prosperous commercial town. At around 9 pm last night, nine bandits suddenly came, holding four guns, and went to four shops: Chen Tongtai Cloth Shop, Mei Taihe Sundries Shop, He Zhentai Salt Shop, and Xia Guangtai General Store, and looted them extensively, losing more than 500 yuan in foreign currency and several hundred yuan in goods and clothing. An elderly couple surnamed Xia were beaten on the head by the bandits, and blood flowed profusely. After looting to their hearts' content, the bandits fled east. The townspeople chased after them, and the Shuang Gou Township Self-Defense Corps in the vicinity heard the alarm and fired many shots, capturing two bandits, Yue Da Ma, etc., on the spot, as well as two guns. This afternoon at 2 pm, they were escorted to the city along with two private salt boats and two bandits and sent to the county for legal proceedings.

Haimen 114

Security Team Soldiers Beat Car Owner

The Donghai long-distance bus, which runs between Haimen and Qidong, came to Haimen from Qidong the day before yesterday and was passing through Fuan Township in the Sixth District. Several soldiers from the Second Company of the Security Team stationed there wanted to take the bus to Haimen. At that time, the bus was crowded with passengers and there was no space. The car owner Shen Zhiting politely refused. Unexpectedly, the soldiers, without asking the reason, dragged Shen off the bus and beat him at will, then dragged him to the team headquarters, tied him with hemp rope, and forced him to sign a statement of apology. Later, District Chief Bao Zhan of the Sixth District went to bail him out, but Shen suffered serious injuries to his chest and waist. He groaned in bed after returning home, and medicine was ineffective, and his life was in danger. Yesterday, Shen's family specially petitioned the county government to investigate and handle the case according to law.

Xiaoshan 115

Husband and Wife Quarrel Over Gambling Money Leads to Tragedy

Tu Jizeng, a resident of You Tu, a place in southern Xiaoshan, and his wife both like to gamble. On the 27th of this month, the couple had a quarrel over gambling money. Tu's wife, Jiang, was known as a shrew. In the afternoon, they fought again. His wife rushed to the kitchen and threw a kitchen knife at her husband's head, hitting his brain directly. Brain matter flowed out, and he immediately fell to the ground and died. Seeing this, neighbors took up for him and detained the shrew and reported the case to the county government for investigation and handling.
