Women's Garden

Looking Forward and Backward 297

— Zi

The years of the twenty-third year of the Republic (1934), with the wheel of time of panic and turmoil, quietly passed away.

On this New Year's Eve, everyone can't help but think forward and backward!

I dare not ask about national matters, and I disdain to talk about personal trifles. As a woman, I am more concerned about women's affairs, and I will summarize the women's affairs of this year:

This year, the women's world was particularly honored to be appointed as special commissioners for promoting domestic products. However, unwelcome news came frequently. The import of foreign goods increased throughout the year. As a result, the public felt resentful and criticized women for not being ambitious. But actually, by understanding the world economy and observing the domestic situation, we know that the external pressure is great and the internal resistance is 奥. The occurrence of this phenomenon is also inevitable. It is unfair to place this difficult task on women who are scattered and under great pressure.

In March and April, Nanchang mobilized the New Life Movement, and there was an order prohibiting women from wearing strange clothes. However, in large cities, fashionable expressions were prevailing, with bare breasts and fluttering dresses. In poor rural areas, there were also noble women with elaborate clothing. There was a great tendency for those who prohibit to prohibit themselves, and those who promote to promote themselves.

Since "Germany" and "Italy" shouted out the slogan "Women Go Home," China has also re-advocated the education of good wives and mothers. However, on the one hand, due to the bankruptcy of the countryside and the depression of the cities, a large number of women abandoned their homes and fled, but they had the regret of not being able to return!

Revival is a new trick this year. With the flames of revival, the concept of chastity has been re-promoted and rewarded. This is a major setback in the voice of women's liberation!

Secondly, with the overall economic panic, human feelings suddenly changed, and women's suicides were often heard. This is another shocking fact.

The above are all a record of this year's women's affairs, which can also be regarded as women's fleeting fortune!

What is barely satisfactory is the success of the suffrage movement, but this remains to be seen whether the facts can be used.

Next year is said to be the year of the child. During the year of the child, the problem of child-rearing must be solved! Everyone knows that without solving the problem of child-rearing, women will not get true liberation, so on the eve of the upcoming year of the child, I have deep hope!

Summary of the Women's National Products Year 298

— Jingbo

The year of the Republic of China's 23rd year, designated as the Women's National Products Year, has slipped away like an arrow!

Following the "September 18th Incident," a wave of boycotts against Japanese goods surged across the nation. For a time, Japanese trade with China declined, and Japanese capital felt threatened. On one hand, Japan used dumping tactics to counter the anti-Japanese movement. On the other hand, unscrupulous merchants, driven by profit, willingly acted as accomplices, substituting Japanese goods with fake trademarks to evade inspection and punishment, selling and transporting them in secret during the height of the boycott. As a result, North and Southwest China, without large-scale boycotts, remained full of cheap and attractive Japanese products. Unfortunately, the boycott not only intensified the sales of British goods at the time, revealing the inherent flaws of the movement but also gradually faded after the 22nd year due to various pressures. In its place arose the "National Products Year," advocating the use of domestic goods under the slogan of "increasing domestic production."

National industrialists and entrepreneurs declared, "To put domestic goods on the path of increased production, reduce the surplus of foreign goods, and curb the sales of Japanese goods through the enthusiastic support of women, it may be possible to make unscrupulous merchants, driven by conscience, abandon their actions that harm national interests." In other words, the so-called Women's National Products Year was an attempt by national industrialists and entrepreneurs, with the encouragement and assistance of the government, to promote the development and stimulation of their capital through this slogan.

Thus, the 23rd year of the Republic of China was designated as the "Women's National Products Year."

National product exhibitions were held in various cities across the country, from Shanghai, Hangzhou, Nanjing, Changsha, Xi'an, and fashion shows were performed in several places in Shanghai and Nanjing, decorating the year with all kinds of dazzling activities. But what was the result of the Women's National Products Year? Perhaps the pockets of individual industrialists and merchants were slightly fuller? But did the entire national industry "put domestic goods on the path of increased production, reduce the surplus of foreign goods, and curb the sales of Japanese goods"? According to customs statistics, from January to October of this year, our national foreign trade deficit was over 430 million yuan. Meanwhile, the yarn and rubber industries are in danger, and recently flour mills have also reduced production (中华日报, December 3rd). Newspaper reports of Japanese goods dumping are filled with alarming news of increased dumping.

Naturally, this situation cannot be remedied by simply "promoting national products," nor is it merely the result of a "five-minute craze" that has subsided. In essence, in China, which is dominated by imperialist economic forces, it is almost impossible to develop national capital. Since the gradual stabilization of various imperialist powers after the European War, they have re-concentrated capital and intensified their efforts in China. The increasing decline of China's most important industry—the textile industry—is clear evidence of this.

The characteristics of China's economy are two-fold: on one hand, the restraint of imperialist economy, and on the other hand, the shackles of feudal forces. Imperialism and China's feudal forces collude and support each other, forming two powerful forces that attack from both sides. China's national industries cannot withstand the competition of imperialism or the devastation of feudal remnants. China's national industry not only cannot expand reproduction, but it cannot even recover simple reproduction, resulting in the decline of industrial production and agriculture. In addition, droughts, floods, and the more or less political fragmentation caused by local warlords, numerous overlapping taxes, chaotic currency systems and huge differences in domestic exchange rates, the lack of uniform standards of weights and measures, and nominal tariff systems all contribute to the fact that China's industries not only cannot develop but are shrinking and even bankrupt.

First, consider from the perspective of production: Heavy industry is the foundation of a modern country, and 90% of China's coal and iron are enterprises of British and Japanese capital. As for China's light industry, the textile industry, known as the king of industries, is experiencing closures, shutdowns, reduced production, and inventory problems. Firstly, Chinese capital and technology are woefully inadequate. The majority of foreign-owned yarn mills in China are Japanese, and the strength of Japanese capital and technological improvements are enough to drag Chinese yarn mills into the waves of decline. In terms of management methods, Japanese mills operate day and night, with a consistent number of spindles running, maintaining balance. Even under the same conditions, with the same number of spindles, Japanese mills produce more than Chinese mills. Chinese yarn mills, on the other hand, have more fixed capital but insufficient circulating capital, stockpiled raw cotton, production restrictions, and backward technology, leaving them with no choice but to close down, shut down, or reduce production. In particular, foreign capital is abundant, and the actual control is entirely in the hands of foreigners. The Chinese production sector is mixed with a lot of foreign capital, and yarn mills use foreign cotton, flour mills use foreign wheat, etc., trapping Chinese production in a semi-colonial dependency, making development impossible. In addition, the lack of tariff autonomy allows foreign goods to flood in like a tide. At the same time, foreign factories in China are not only exempt from import duties on their products, but foreigners also enjoy the benefits of the Three-Link Certificate when purchasing local goods in the interior, which exempts them from levies and taxes along the way, while Chinese merchants do not. Moreover, Chinese merchants purchase foreign cotton through the hands of foreigners, resulting in yet another layer of exploitation. Naturally, the production cost of foreign goods is lower than that of Chinese goods. Therefore, under these favorable conditions, foreign goods are dumped at low prices, while Chinese national industrial production is permanently mired in a declining state.

Secondly, consider from the perspective of the market: China does not have a unified market. On the basis of a divided economic foundation, coupled with the special interests of various imperialist powers, a situation of market division has been created in China. In Guangdong, in April, the southwest authorities passed a three-year industrial construction plan, implementing exclusive sales of products such as sugar and cement, and promulgated thirteen articles of tariff rules for collecting protective taxes on goods imported from outside the province, with the tax rate reaching as high as 50%. The leader of Hunan, in the name of maintaining the provincial first yarn factory, adopted the method of market blockade, set up a cotton management office, and restricted the import of cotton yarn produced by yarn mills in Shanghai and Wuhan into the province. Shanxi has recently implemented a ban on the import of matches from other provinces. The conclusion of these facts is that localism and protectionist forces, following the economic interests of various imperialist powers, are leading to the segmentation of the domestic market; balancing a province's trade deficit by dividing the market is also an attempt to eliminate the increasingly expanding financial crisis; this is precisely the will of imperialism. The intensification of the capital war of various imperialist powers in China increasingly demands the delineation of specific spheres of influence, and the loss of Northeast China is a clear indication of the beginning of the carve-up. In this way, the entire structure of the national economy is becoming more backward and declining, and national industries can only decline.

Under these circumstances, promoting domestic goods purely from the standpoint of boycotting Japanese goods is active. But from the perspective of the development of the Chinese economy, this function becomes very passive. Obviously, it is impossible for China's declining and fragmented national industry to save itself from its doom merely by promoting domestic goods or by relying on the weak stimulation of the Women's National Products Year. In reality, it is a kind of weak illusion.

Who are the supporters of the Women's National Products Year? They are high-class and middle-class women. These people have more purchasing power among women. However, their enthusiasm is only for Europeanization, modernity, and decoration, so their purchasing power does not increase the productivity of domestic goods. Facts prove that the import of cosmetics and toys in the first ten months of this year reached more than three million yuan, which broke all historical records. And for the women of the lower classes, unemployment, hunger, and bankruptcy are their relationship and response to the Women's National Products Year.

Therefore, it is inevitable that this year's Women's National Products Year will not be very effective. Nothing to be surprised about.

A Self-Description by a "Social Person" 299

— Li Zhishan

The Lessons Given to Me by Family, School, and Society

Although my family is a "scholarly family for generations," and my grandfather and father were influential gentlemen in the entire village and within dozens of miles, we were completely in the working class in terms of living standards because of poverty. My late mother was an old-fashioned woman with both talent and virtue, but in life, she was so poor that she needed to spin and weave to earn a few strings of cash to buy food to avoid starvation. How could a little girl in such an environment reach her current state? Let me describe it below:

How I Got the Opportunity to Study

How did I get the opportunity to study? (1) My father was a scholar with rich thoughts and far-sighted vision, and his philosophy was to always take the "lead in everything." (2) After my only younger brother died, my parents had no sons, so they wanted to cultivate a daughter. (3) I declared to my parents that if they allowed me to go to Tianjin to study, I would definitely be able to bear the responsibility of a son in supporting them. So my father immediately sold the only ten acres of land to provide me with funds to go to Tianjin Normal School to study. This was in the second year of the Republic of China. At that time, the atmosphere in the north was still very closed, and I was the only woman in Yanshan County to study outside.

The Influence of School on Me

Since I overcame all kinds of difficulties to get the opportunity to study, I naturally worked hard desperately. When I first arrived at school, I didn't understand anything, and everyone laughed at me as a country bumpkin. But in the second semester, I became the representative figure of my class. At the first debate held by the school, even though I was in the lowest grade, I was assigned as one of the debaters. At the moment when the judges calculated the scores at the end of the debate, I automatically ran to the stage to give a speech to the whole school on the benefits of the debate and encourage the students to participate enthusiastically. It was this that I encountered a major setback: the principal immediately announced to the public that I did not understand the rules, and before taking the stage, I had to ask the chairman for permission to speak, and I could only speak after the chairman allowed it. Alas! As a child who had just come out of the countryside, and with no training in gatherings at school, how could I understand? Being hit by this big nail in public gave me too much of a blow. From then on, until graduation, I never participated in any school activities. Thinking about it now, this had a great impact on my ability to train. However, I was able to obtain relatively rich scientific knowledge in school, which provided a foundation for my further study. So this stage of life is worth mentioning here in particular.

Teaching and Participating in the "May Fourth" Movement

After studying at the normal school for five years, I graduated in the summer of the seventh year of the Republic of China and was assigned to teach at the attached primary school. At that time, the highest salary for primary school teachers was 30 yuan per month, but in order to actually bear the responsibility of supporting my parents, I also worked as a tutor in a family and taught courses at other schools, so I actually had an income of more than 50 yuan per month. My private life was also very thrifty. Apart from three yuan for food and three yuan for pocket money, I gave all the money to my father. An income of 40 to 50 yuan per month in the countryside was really amazing, so everyone was willing to send their daughters to school, and the atmosphere was refreshed. Until now, I am still bearing the responsibility of a son in supporting my family.

At that time, my state of mind was extremely happy. A daughter could also be a son, and I won a breath for women. Although my body and mind were tired, my spirit was happy. In order to fulfill the responsibility of a son to my parents, and because I was afraid of being a daughter-in-law—the life of a daughter-in-law in the north is the most bitter, and I had personally seen my late mother suffer all kinds of bad treatment to the point of death—I vowed not to marry. I planned to remain single for the rest of my life and serve in the education field, believing that it was the most appropriate plan for the country, for the family, and for myself.

In May of the eighth year of the Republic of China, the "May Fourth" Movement broke out. Stimulated by my own strong heart and the desire to compete with men, I organized the Tianjin Women's Patriotic Association with classmates from my alma mater, which was the beginning of my participation in social movements. In the process of being in charge of the work of the Patriotic Association, I still encountered some difficulties as when I first arrived at school from the countryside, and I understood how to deal with society and how to lead the masses. Ah! The "May Fourth" Movement taught me too much: it liberated my thinking, broadened my horizons, and made me dissatisfied with the current society. I wanted to create a new life, and simply sticking to the industry was not a perfect life, and I needed to create a career. Single life is against nature, and marriage can still support parents, and I don't have to be a daughter-in-law under my in-laws. So my view of life changed: I regard the occupation as a need for material life, the cause as a sustenance for spiritual life, and marriage as something that should have the spirit of singleness, but not the reality of singleness. The scope of occupation is naturally not limited to primary school teachers, and the scope of career is determined to be engaged in women's movement and patriotic movement for life.

Me in Career and Cause

I have been engaged in career life for seventeen years now. During this period, I have worked as a primary school teacher, a middle school dean, an editor for daily, biweekly, and monthly publications, and a staff member of a party official agency. Among them, the life of a party official was the most bitter. When I was a member of the Shanghai Municipal Party Executive Committee in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, I experienced many factional disputes within the party and some base and disgusting things that turned friends into enemy parties, which are unbearable to recall. Therefore, I felt that I was the least suitable for political life. Among them, the job of editor was the most interesting to me, because what I edited were women's publications, and there was also a component of cause in it.

In terms of career, since the "May Fourth" Movement, I have been engaged in patriotic movements and have published Tianjin Women's Daily, organized the Female Star Society, published the Female Star Biweekly, and founded the Female Star Women's Remedial School with female comrades who were full of revolutionary consciousness. Since the success of the Northern Expedition of the Kuomintang, I have repeatedly awakened women's ideology organizations in Nanjing, Shanghai, and other places, promoting the success of the national revolution on the one hand, and realizing the equality of men and women's rights on the other hand. I am really ashamed that I have not achieved anything so far! Among the careers I have participated in, only one type of Women's Resonance Monthly still exists, but what kind of help does this give to the actual career? Because I feel the poverty of spiritual life, this year I and my comrades in Beijing organized the Women's Cultural Promotion Association, seeking to unite with like-minded sisters, starting with solving the suffering of women themselves, and then expanding them into a powerful team of women's movement and national revolution.

Thoughts After Entering Society

Seventeen years after entering society, I feel that society is cold, selfish, and intolerant of Nora-style women. When a woman runs to society, she is bound by unequal etiquette and establishment forces in all aspects. People in society are most likely to slander women, and they are accustomed to slandering them with sexual relations. In this male society where no one is a government official, if a woman is promoted because of the promotion of a superior, the words of sexual slander will come out. Look, which of the women who are in higher positions now has not been slandered? This shows the lack of sincerity of society towards women. From the Xinhai Revolution to the present, women have received the sincere support of men in about three periods: namely, the three revolutionary tense periods of the Xinhai Revolution, the "May Fourth" Movement, and the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army. As soon as the revolutionary atmosphere slackens, the concept of playing with women arises, and even various sets of circles are set up to deceive women, and after women enter the circle, they create a big reason for laughter and slander to punish them. Apart from the above three periods, women who have entered society can be said to be struggling in the dark under the heavy clouds every day. I am also a young general in this struggling group.

December 25th of the 23rd year of the Republic of China at the Women's Resonance Society

From the Appointment of the Fourth Legislative Yuan Members to the Women's Movement 300

— Zhen Yi

On the 26th of this month, the Central Political Committee appointed 86 members of the fourth Legislative Yuan, of which 67 were re-elected from the third session. Neither of the original female legislators was re-elected, and two other people were appointed instead. The number of female legislators in previous sessions has not only not increased, but has also decreased by one compared to the first and second sessions.

Some people may think that this is a retreat of the women's movement, and that the women's participation in politics has been going on for so many years, and the results are only like this. In fact, this view is wrong.

If it is really believed that this is a retreat of the women's movement, then the women's movement is only a movement to push a few women onto the political stage, and not a movement to seek the liberation of the masses of women. In this China, where the poison of etiquette and teaching still exists, the economic power is completely in the hands of men, and all politics, education, and legislation are centered on men. Women are either playthings or slaves. Although capitalism has invaded, it has absorbed many women to participate in production and given some women the opportunity to obtain occupations. However, the shackles of women have not been reduced, and even the atmosphere of women returning to the family is becoming more and more intense. Under these circumstances, it is impossible to rely solely on a few female legislators appointed by the government to liberate the masses of women from top to bottom. Not to mention that it is difficult for only two or three female legislators to pass proposals, even if more women participate, if they are speaking on behalf of the masses, then men can also use various methods to suppress or exclude them in order to defend their own interests. Therefore, the real women's movement should be based on the majority of awakened women, unite rural women and housewives, and seek the thorough liberation of women from the bottom up.

Women's participation in politics is not absolutely useless. If women have strong groups and strong forces, they may be able to obtain some welfare by means of political power. Otherwise, participation in politics away from the masses has nothing to do with the entire women's movement except to improve personal status and position.

Santa Claus and the Women's National Products Year 301

— Qian

My first understanding of Santa Claus was when I entered a church school at the age of thirteen and celebrated my first Christmas. I remember it was at two o'clock in the afternoon on December 25th, and as soon as the bell rang, everyone in the school swarmed into the gymnasium. I saw a costumed Western old man standing on the judging platform, wearing a red robe, with white hair and beard made entirely of cotton; according to old classmates, that was Santa Claus, who would give us Christmas presents.

Soon, sure enough, everyone in the school, from the principal to the janitor, received a red paper bag from the hands of this strange old man. Eager people opened the paper bag before returning to their seats. Some got foreign writing pads and a pencil, six Bs and seven Bs, and some got foreign stationery and envelopes, and some got foreign erasers and foreign penholders. Christmas comes to the world majestically every year, and Santa Claus brings gifts to everyone every year. But as time goes by, the gifts have also changed every year. Gradually, some classmates got a box of foreign face powder, and some got a long box of foreign talcum powder.

Just like not long ago, classmates had a deep love for foreign pencils, foreign stationery and envelopes, and foreign erasers and penholders, and scrambled to buy them out of their pockets, the big and small goblins had a deadly love for foreign face powder and talcum powder. Now, not only is the once-popular borneol talcum powder ignored, but even the face powder that was once considered indispensable, if anyone is still using it, everyone seems to have made a pact that they will regard that person as a bumpkin, as a country girl. Just at this moment, Santa Claus changed his tricks again. This time, he brought some colorful, brilliant glass bead necklaces. And for many years to come, the gifts have been changing every year, from foreign velvet ropes, foreign silk threads, and foreign clothing lace, to foreign wallets and foreign fake bracelets, and then to jeweled hairpins, brooches, and foreign fake gemstone rings. Then there was a big change in the world: wearing red gold necklaces, rings, and red gold brooches and bracelets is a bumpkin, is a country girl: the foundation of fashion is foreign jewelry again.

As time goes by, according to my calculations, the students of my alma mater, as well as the girls of various foreign schools across the country, have received the gift of foreign gifts from Santa Claus for nearly twenty years now. According to reports published in various newspapers, this year, which is the year of promoting national products the most, the total import of cosmetics, clothing, and foreign jewelry for women in our country has reached more than two million yuan. However, recently, many patriotic people, worried about the outflow of money, are already writing articles about sending women the National Products Year, wanting women not to regard the end of the Women's National Products Year as the end of their responsibilities, and should catch up quickly to recover our country's economic rights and interests. Not only that, some smart people actually pin this slim ray of hope on the Student National Products Year next year. I think this kind of hope will eventually be just hope. Don't you see, the puppets of the pioneers of various foreign goods—Santa Claus—their puppeteers are gradually multiplying there, one generation is more like one generation, they have passed from father to son, and son to grandson, and now they have reached the era of great-grandsons and great-great-grandsons. Its deep-rooted power can never be killed by a few words of "patriotism" "patriotism" and a few "what year" "what year." Everyone open their eyes and see more clearly!

Tianjin Women's World 302

— Zi Tu

Tianjin, often called "Little Shanghai," indeed has a bit of a seaside feel. Its industry and commerce are central in North China, and it is, without a doubt, a transportation hub. Western-style buildings with large window openings stand tall, and cars speed along asphalt roads. Dance halls are filled with music and dancing all night long—these are all signs of a bustling metropolis.

Tianjin women, standing on the level playing field, are immersed in a competition of beauty and glamour—of course, this refers to a segment of the population. The so-called socialites and celebrities are keen on participating in various singing and dancing troupes. They sometimes have the honor of participating in naming or groundbreaking ceremonies, cutting ribbons and tossing champagne glasses amidst cheers, providing material for the illustrated magazines the next day. At times, the clever owners of department stores or domestic goods shops specially invite young ladies or wives from prominent families to model clothes, showcasing new silks or sweaters. The styles of these clothes leave ordinary people in a state of baffled bewilderment.

Fortunately, there are no dance bans or instructions prohibiting men and women from holding hands here. People have a considerable amount of freedom. Many dance enthusiasts from Beiping long for Tianjin's dance halls, where there are open dance hostesses and ten-story Western-style buildings, and all the facilities follow Shanghai's lead. In the music, people forget the sorrows of the world, and the faces with red lips or shiny hair are always smiling.

Many university girls are also working hard. The girls at Nankai University are always looked upon with a bit more respect, perhaps because of the school spirit and curriculum, but compared to the girls at Hebei Women's Normal School, they already have quite a bit of an aristocratic air. The pastimes that female students are into are ball games, ice skating, and swimming. A love of sports has almost become a universal hobby for female students in North China, unlike the girls in Jiangnan, who are much more fond of staying indoors. Speaking of entertainment, one cannot forget the gambling in Tianjin. In addition to cards and poker, there are also large roulette wheels and jai alai courts... and these venues feature wealthy wives and young concubines. Most of these bustling places are located in the concessions, and Tianjin has many concessions.

There are also quite a few women who are teachers and small office workers. They live a simple and stable life, and after having enough to eat and wear, going to the park or seeing a movie is considered an extra treat.

Tianjin's brothels exist both openly and secretly. Prostitutes who are also dancers are the ones who easily attract a large clientele. In the hidden brothels, there are cries stifled by life's pressures. On street corners or in playgrounds, they tug at men's sleeves, and laughter flies from their blackened eyes.

In the Chinese territory, women who are coolies or laborers can be seen building Western-style buildings, driving piles, or carrying mud and tiles, leaving their children to the side. The factory chimneys in Tianjin never stop, and some female workers have to run for several miles from their homes to the concessions. In "three-no-care" areas like the City God Temple, there are women selling sweets and toys all year round, and women performing Bengbeng opera. Tianjin women who love to sing the waterfront ballad waddle along, their bellies protruding.

Along the streets, there are seamstresses quietly sewing and mending, and, of course, there are always beggars constantly pleading.

Extreme revelry covers up the spreading misery, but in reality, it can't cover it all.

Random Thoughts at the Year's End 303

— Bing Ying

Time seems to have passed in a dream. In the blink of an eye, 1934 is drawing to a close, lightning-fast time!

People are truly like waves in the sea, not even knowing their own movements, their own future! I, too, am like a wave drifting to this cold island nation! Who would have thought that I would spend 1934 in Tokyo?

Here, I have met many friends who are diligently studying Chinese literature, and I have also met several female comrades who are working hard in cultural work and the women's liberation movement. They are all pioneers of the era, warriors striving to create a new society. I am very happy. Although looking out from my lonely little room, the earth is so cold, gloomy, and a vast expanse of white snow, my spirit is as excited as spring!

Whether it is day or night, I never dare to rest. I feel that life is too short, there is so much knowledge to seek, so much to do. Even a minute of time should not be allowed to pass lightly, let alone be wasted.

I often think that women have more work to do than men, and that women bear a greater mission than men, because in addition to working hard in cultural undertakings, we must also strive for the liberation movement of oppressed women. Not to mention all the trivial matters in the family, which are also the responsibility of women. Therefore, all female writers should bear at least two responsibilities: on the one hand, to work hard in cultural work, and on the other hand, to strive for the liberation movement of oppressed women.

Except for one or two countries, women all over the world are in a state of oppression. They are just as human as men, but because of the unequal social and economic system, they live an inhuman life, a hellish and dark life. Female comrades who are working hard in cultural work, only women themselves deeply understand the suffering of women, and deeply sympathize with them. In fact, we should not say that we sympathize with them, because we ourselves are in the same state of oppression as they are, and our own lives are also as unfree, as tragic, painful, and pitiful as theirs. We must stand up our spirits and do the entire women's liberation movement of the oppressed! In our creations, we must also describe more of the lives of the laboring class women, their suffering and their demands.

1934 is coming to an end! Let everyone quietly think about it, what have we contributed to art in this year, what have we contributed to society? I think perhaps everyone has feelings? Everyone thinks that time has passed too quickly, another year has ended, the work they had planned has not been completed, society is still a dark society, our lives are still unfree lives, countless millions of oppressed people have sacrificed in hunger and cold, in the midst of artillery fire! Writing to this point, I stopped writing, and respectfully offer the 1934 memorial to the Chinese masses who sacrificed in the struggle!

The New Year is coming soon! I don't feel as happy as I did in my childhood, but I am not sad either. Let the past ice pass, we must seize the present, and even more tightly grasp the future! The cold and gloomy winter will go away with the end of the year, and the warm spring will give us the strength to move forward, to strive to create a new culture, and a new life for women, my dear comrades!

End of 1934 in Tokyo

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Welcome New Year Special Issue (One)

Chinese Literature in the Past Year 304

— Zhu Xinhua

This year is called a "Magazine Year," and among the more than six hundred privately published periodicals, there seem to be quite a few that focus on "pure literature." However, no matter who you ask, they will say that the Chinese literary scene in 1934 was not very lively. Speaking of literary theory, there have been no major or truly worthwhile books on literary principles, literary criticism, and literary history published this year. Nor have there been any systematic debates on general literary theory. There have only been short essays published in the "Editorial Notes" of various literary journals, and debates sparked in the back pages of newspapers on issues such as the "Beijing School" and "Shanghai School." Of course, some of these raised relatively important issues, such as philology and literary heritage, which are undoubtedly of great significance. However, even in these debates, the theoretical expression has been relatively weak. As for creative works, that is even more difficult to talk about. Facts tell us that this year, apart from a few short stories published in various literary journals, there are almost no good full-length single-volume works to be found. Not to mention new writers, even some established writers such as Mao Dun, Lu Xun, and Yu Dafu have not produced anything this year. Perhaps because of the need to fill the void in the creative world, the most common works published in single volumes this year are "Selected Works of So-and-So" or "Selected Short Stories," and so on.

However, the Chinese literary scene in 1934 was not entirely barren, with nothing at all. Although the expressions in both theory and creative works were very weak, there were still some expressions. Moreover, in the theoretical aspect, because several important issues were raised and discussed, even if it cannot yield any results at present, it has a great driving force for the development of Chinese literature. Therefore, in order to understand the past and look forward to the future, it is still necessary for us to review the Chinese literary scene in the past year.

First, let's talk about the several issues that caused controversy in the Chinese literary scene this year.

Everyone knows that the essay was the first to make a splash in the Chinese literary scene this year. With the great popularity of essays, a war between essays and long articles was triggered. Humor master Lin Yutang took the lead in starting "The World," specializing in advocating essays, declaring that essays could "talk about the universe" or "talk about flies," truly capable of anything. But those on the other side said: "Essays are only suitable for expressing flies, not suitable for expressing the universe. To explain the universe, and thus solve the problems of the universe, long and detailed articles are necessary. Short essays cannot handle this. No matter what, a genius at writing essays cannot explain the origin and evolution of the universe in a short essay. Of course, essays can also explain a part of the problem of the universe, and can also grasp a certain point to explain the entire universe, but that is all. It still cannot be considered capable of explaining and thus solving the big problems of the universe and life. If an essay writer wants to mark out a cosmic or social problem, attempting to explain and thus solve it in a short text, the result will certainly be a failure." (See "The Great America Evening News" May 11th)

Those who advocated essays, because essays are valued for being short and concise, also issued the argument that "brevity is precious in writing." But opponents also refuted this: "...Even using tens of millions of words to write about a person's psychological changes within a day would not be considered redundant. And Wu Cheng'en's original "Journey to the West" is even more verbose than Zhu Dingchen and Yang Zhihe's abridged versions. If someone were to abridge "Dream of the Red Chamber" into a two- or three-thousand-word excerpt, wouldn't the essence be completely lost, and only the dross remain! The so-called modern short story is not only valued for being short. Many important short stories are often more than twenty or thirty thousand words.

··········

"Primitive history used a few words or dozens of words to record a person's life, but today's novels write a story of one day into tens of millions of words. Is this evolution or regression? It can be understood without further explanation." (See "Literature" Volume 2, Number 6)

This is indeed a powerful refutation of the essay masters who excessively elevated the status of essays and advocated "brevity is precious in writing."

However, later, there was also a divergence within the scope of essays: on the one hand, there were essays with new content represented by "Taibai," and on the other hand, there were the so-called "expressing aspirations" essays represented by "The World," which attempted to revive classical Chinese. Although the former has not yet produced any achievements, the ideas and emotions it conveys are relatively progressive. The latter, on the other hand, uses the feelings, letters, and doggerel poems of several old-fashioned professors in Beiping to show off themselves, and its use is only for leisure after tea and wine. Master Yutang himself said it well: "The bi-monthly (referring to his essay bi-monthly | author) has about 40,000 words, just enough to read and relax for two hours in the evening. After reading, roll up the quilt and go to sleep. When I get up tomorrow, I will still work in the office, copy relief, and issue notices as a principal, feeling a hundred times more energetic, just like someone who goes to a restaurant for a small drink. The taste of fresh bamboo shoots fried with flat beans from last night is still on the tip of my tongue." (See "The World" Fourth Issue)

Following the debate on the essay issue, the issue of language was raised. Among these, the first to attract people's attention was Mr. Chen Zizhan's article "Classical Chinese | Vernacular Chinese | Mass Language" in "Free Talk" on June 18th. Since then, publications such as "Trend" in "China Daily," "Local Supplement" in "Shen Bao," "New Linguistic Forest," "Taibai," "Social Daily," "Social Monthly," and other publications have been caught up in the vortex of this debate. Almost all of the country's new and old writers participated in this debate. If all the writings on this issue were completely collected, I think there would be at least two thick volumes. However, due to space and other reasons, I cannot introduce and critique the opinions of all parties here. Please readers study them yourselves. Here, I will just summarize the main opinions of the various parties:

Some people say that classical Chinese is concise and valuable, so they attempt to revive classical Chinese;

Another group advocates preserving the ideas of the "May Fourth" era and supports vernacular Chinese;

Still another group are eclecticists, saying that classical Chinese and vernacular Chinese each have their own advantages, advocating the use of both together;

There are also those who feel that classical Chinese and vernacular Chinese are both outdated, advocating the establishment of a mass language: and further abolishing square characters, adopting Romanized spelling, to thoroughly transform Chinese language and writing.

Among these several opinions, who is right? I cannot make a simple judgment here with the words "yes" or "no," but rather hope that the readers will study them in detail themselves.

Of course, there are also "the issue of accepting literary heritage," "the issue of translating foreign works," and "the issue of why China has not been able to produce great works." These are all important issues raised in the Chinese literary scene this year. However, also due to space limitations, I cannot explain them one by one here. Now, for what is necessary for us,

Page 20

Amateur Chat

General Overview of the World and China in 1934 305

— Xu Zhi

Time flies relentlessly forward. Last year has just passed, and this year is already coming to an end. I remember when we first placed the 1934 calendar on our desks, some prophet predicted that a military leader and a politician would die within the year. Indeed, German General Hindenburg passed away this year, and Little Napoleon Dollfuss was assassinated in Vienna. King Alexander of Yugoslavia and French Foreign Minister Barthou were also shot in Marseille. The beloved King Albert also fell off a cliff and died an unnatural death, and Soviet Central Committee member Kirov was also assassinated just days ago. This doubly proves the accuracy of our prophet's predictions!

In reality, the world is so vast, and there are so many people called politicians and military leaders. Wouldn't one or two politicians or military leaders die within a year, especially in these crisis-ridden times? However, since the prophet's prediction has been proven, there is no need for us to comment further!

Just as it was predicted that someone would inevitably die in 1934, many political and military experts have made equally startling predictions: that World War II will inevitably break out in 1936! They even say with relish that once the war breaks out, a certain country's warships will sail to a certain place, and another country's air force will bomb a certain city; at first, a certain country will definitely be defeated, and then it will inevitably turn defeat into victory... Although we are not yet sure whether such fortune-telling calculations are completely accurate, judging from the many important international events of the past year, the crisis of war is indeed approaching us day by day. Please flip through the past calendar! The constant disturbances in Vienna, the repeated mobilization of Italian troops, the purges by the German and Soviet authorities, the turmoil in Spain, the urgency of the situation in Central Europe and the Balkans, the sound of cannons in the Chaco War in South America, the bankruptcy of the preliminary Anglo-American-Japanese naval conference, the deterioration of Soviet-Japanese relations... These great facts tell us that the god of war is like a fast airplane, sometimes circling in Central Europe, sometimes flying over the Pacific Ocean. No one can say when it will land and where!

Smart friends, you must know that whether the prophet's predictions have been proven by facts, or whether the calculations of politicians and military leaders are accurate, these do not have much research significance; however, the fact that prophets and politicians insist on predicting what kind of people will die within a year, and insist on calculating the time of the outbreak of the world war, doesn't this precisely indicate the nervousness of the general public? Yes, on the eve of a major event, the general public is always nervous. This is a general description of the world in 1934.

What about China? According to the regulations of those enthusiastic about the national goods movement, 1934 is the "Women's National Goods Year," and according to the literati, this year is also the "Magazine Year." In fact, both are reasonable. In fact, within this year, women have indeed made considerable efforts to promote national goods. In addition to formal expressions such as meetings and parades, one can imagine the achievements of the national goods movement this year simply by looking at the bustling scene of the national goods department stores on Nanjing Road; at the same time, it is said that more than 1,000 magazines were published this year. Compared with previous years, this year can certainly be said to be the "Magazine Year." However, in the "Women's National Goods Year," according to reports, the import of various cosmetics is still particularly high, and the amount of import surplus seems to be still rising; at the same time, in the "Magazine Year," although there are more than 1,000 magazines, compared with other advanced countries, it is still very, very few, and even among these more than 1,000 magazines, very few are really worth reading. In the past year, apart from the issue of "short essays" and "long essays," it seems that no more satisfactory works have been produced on the literary scene. All of this fully illustrates that our efforts in 1934 were not enough, and we need another "National Goods Year" and another "Magazine Year"! Friends, come! Concentrate all our strength, let's stir up the huge waves of the nation, let's stir up the raging tide of the Chinese sea!

At the same time, if we look at the situation of Chinese society under the oppression of imperialism in the past year, it is also frightening. Looking up, almost all we see are the wounds of the masses, and all we hear are the tragic cries of the masses! The widespread floods and droughts across the country have already caused countless victims to be unable to survive; under the onslaught of the economic downturn, countless factories and workshops have closed down this year, countless shops have declared liquidation, and countless unemployed people have been added. This situation is again warning us how we should continue to fight!

Friends, the world situation is so urgent, and all the circumstances in China are telling us that we must continue to work hard and struggle. In this regard, how will you settle the past and plan for the future? Isn't this a very serious question?

It is still necessary to briefly talk about Chinese literary creation in the past year.

After searching the bookstores on the Four Horses Road, I finally found two novella (or even novels) published this year: Shen Congwen's "Border Town" and Lao She's "Little Slope's Birthday." But I just want to talk about the former here; as for the latter, I will talk about it when I have the opportunity.

In "Border Town," the author first tells us that on the border of western Hunan there is a small mountain town called "Chadong." Here, there is a small stream, an old man, a girl, and a yellow dog managing a ferryboat on the stream, constantly ferrying passengers back and forth every day. The old man and the girl are both very kind and gentle, and they are very faithful to their duties. They don't charge money from passengers, and sometimes even if the passengers want to give the old man some money, he will absolutely refuse, and even get so anxious that he will quarrel with the passengers if they insist on giving money. Even the yellow dog is very understanding. As soon as the boat reaches the shore, it will jump ashore and use its mouth to pull the rope for the old man. Then the author tries to depict how kind the customs and human feelings of this "Border Town" Chadong are, how pure and kind, loyal and gentle the general public is. All the sailors, boat owners, merchants, soldiers, and even prostitutes here are all secure in their professions and willing to help others; here, there is no deception, no disturbance, no cruel and unfair phenomena, only honesty, peace, and the expressions of joy, anger, sorrow, and joy that exist in "general human nature." In the current real situation, this can truly be said to be a "Peach Blossom Spring"!

But all the situations in the "Peach Blossom Spring," and the general way of life in it, existed in Chinese society many years ago. The China of today does not have this world. The China of today is a bankrupt rural economy, and a declining urban industry and commerce. What we see are all phenomena of starvation and cold, deception, and unrest.

Some of the people who live in the real environment of deception and disturbance feel the evil of reality and yearn for the past. If you are willing to go to the countryside and to the older generation of old people, then you will often hear this kind of saying: The past was still good, the Qing Dynasty was good. People at that time were all honest. How could people today be so cunning? Alas, when will a true emperor come out! All the situations in Chadong mentioned above, and the social thought in "Border Town," are reflections of this kind of consciousness.

In order to express this idea, the author constructed a love story, which is the backbone of "Border Town." In the middle of this, the author depicts how Cui Cui, the niece of the loyal old boatman, and the second son of the boat owner Shunshun are in love with each other, but the boat owner's eldest son also loves Cui Cui. Later, because the eldest son felt that he could not compete with his younger brother, he went out to run a business in the lower reaches of the river, but unexpectedly he was drowned on the way; as a result, the boat owner and his second son were not satisfied with the old boatman, thinking that their son and elder brother had been killed because he was meddling; later, the old boatman died, and although the boat owner wanted to marry Cui Cui as his daughter-in-law, his second son had gone out and had not returned, and it was not known when he would return, or whether he would return. Thus, the novel "Border Town" ends. In the middle of this, the author is doing his best to depict the twists and turns of the story line, strengthening the artistic effect of his social thought of anti-expression. But because the social thought he reflects is a social thought that attempts to escape reality, and the world he expresses is not the real world, but the past world, it greatly harms the value of his work; moreover, in many places, we still feel that the author's descriptive power is not enough. For example, when the old boatman dies, the lonely Cui Cui, in addition to crying, does not have any moving expression. In fact, a person who has been stimulated by the greatest pain, especially a person like Cui Cui, does not only cry. Her actions and her psychology are bound to undergo great changes. But the author only expresses this with abstract crying.

If an author's autobiography can also be regarded as a literary work, then here we can cite "Ba Jin's Autobiography."

I do not know Ba Jin, but I like him and admire him. Why? Because, first, he can always be faithful to his beliefs, unlike some of his companions, who jump around casually. Of course, whether his beliefs are entirely correct is still a question that needs to be discussed, but in the current situation of moral corruption, he can always be responsible for the truth he knows, and not jump around casually, which is worthy of admiration. In his autobiography published this year, he still said so firmly: "I have never lost my faith at any time, so I have always endured all this like a tough man. I did not utter a cry of pain. Although my novels sometimes contain deep melancholy, this melancholy has never obscured that ray of light. My love for humanity encourages me and gives me the strength to struggle with everything." This spirit is the first reason why I like Ba Jin. Second, Ba Jin can live and write seriously. He does not leave reality. He often travels and goes deep into the general population to investigate and experience their lives, and then faithfully depicts and contributes them to society. Of course, whether the reality described under his worldview is suitable for the situation and requirements of the objective world is still a problem, but his courage to approach reality and his efforts to be as faithful to reality as possible in his creation are still worthy of our admiration. This is the second reason why I like Ba Jin.

Although "Ba Jin's Autobiography" is very short, it also tells the author's story in Spring. After reading this, one can know a little about the author's childhood life, family situation, and creative process. As for the writing style, because the author is a writer with creative experience, it is also very good. However, one point cannot completely satisfy us, that is, the several major eras that the author has gone through (such as the "Xinhai Revolution," such as the era after 1925) have not been clearly revealed in the middle, thus reducing the social significance of this autobiography.

In addition, it seems that there are quite a few creative things in this year's edition, such as "collections" and "selections." According to what I have seen, there are:

Shen Congwen: "Ru Collection" Life Edition

Lao She: "Catching Up Collection"

Liangyou Edition

Mao Dun: "Tales"

Liangyou Edition

Mu Shiying: "Platinum Female Statue" Modern Edition Zhang Tianyi: "Migration" Liangyou Edition

··········

But my article seems to have been written too long, and I can't comment on these anymore, so let's end it like this.

Chinese Drama in the Past Year 306

— Ms. Zheng Lang

Here I want to make a nationwide narrative. But because I am limited by my personal experience and incomplete materials, there will inevitably be omissions and errors here. I must first ask the readers to forgive me and point out any corrections.

Generally speaking, except for a few places such as Nanjing, the theatrical atmosphere in most parts of the country is very quiet. Due to the determination of the objective environment, the breathing of dramatists often fails to be as free as people imagine. Furthermore, due to the lack of subjective ability, the results of the efforts of the dramatists often fail to be as good as expected. This year, whether from the perspective of drama periodicals, drama disputes, or performances, there has not been a brilliant performance. Now, we might as well make a brief liquidation of these aspects.

(1) The Decline of Drama Periodicals This year is a famous "Magazine Year", but this "Magazine Year" has no relationship with drama. It is rare to see the creation of drama magazines. Although at the end of this 1934, we have already seen the "Modern Drama" monthly magazine edited by four gentlemen, Bao Shiling, He Wu Tieyi, and Lu Si, which was announced in September and October, but the only special drama publication that we have recently worn is this one. In March and April of last year, we found in the bookstore "Performing Arts" founded by a part of Shanghai drama people, but it was only a thin book, and it disappeared after three issues. In other cities in China, it is rare to hear of the creation of single-copy drama magazines. Although there is a "Journal of Drama Studies" published by the "Institute of Chinese Opera and Music" in Peiping, this is not a spoken drama magazine. What they advocate is mainly old dramas, and spoken drama articles are not easy to find in it.

The situation of the drama supplements of newspapers is better, but from a comprehensive examination, it is still not satisfactory. In Shanghai, the "Drama Weekly" (later renamed "Drama Movement") of the Min Bao was discontinued in June for some reason. The "Torch" of the Da Wan Bao did not see any follow-up after publishing an issue of "Drama Garden" not long ago for some reason. The drama weekly edited by Yuan Muzhi of the Zhonghua Daily is now a relatively readable drama publication in the country, which is slightly satisfactory. Its predecessor was "Drama and Film", which was renamed "Drama Weekly" in August and expanded its size to its current form in early September. This publication is currently being converted into a single copy. In addition, the "Drama Edition" of the Social Evening News, which was recently founded, has not attracted people's attention so far, probably because of the newspaper's sales or the content of the publication.

Nanjing is said to be the "Drama Year" this year, but judging from the drama publications that guide the progress of the drama movement, it seems that there are not many achievements to be seen. Ma Yanxiang founded "Drama Weekly" in the Central Daily in June, but this did not add any strength to the Nanjing drama scene. Its content can be said to have no relationship with the Nanjing drama community. This publication rarely publishes even drama reviews and news. In October, Hua Bao founded "Dance Art", "Later Comes First", and the latter is superior to the former in terms of the freshness and richness of content and form.

In the north, drama publications are even more scattered. I have not heard of any decent drama publications in Peiping, the "Ancient Capital" and "Cultural City", this year. Although the "Drama Weekly" edited by Zhang Mingqi of the Tianjin Yong Bao occasionally publishes some readable articles, Tianjin, which is so big, also has "only one". The "Drama Weekly" edited by Yan Zhewu of the Jinan Shandong Min Bao is narrow in size and its content is not very substantial. Other things worth mentioning are rarely seen.

In South China, Guangzhou has always had a very thick theatrical atmosphere. Many drama publications have been published in the past, but this year it seems particularly depressed, scattered and without any expression.

(2) Controversy 1 There are very few heated disputes in the drama world this year, which reflects the current

Stage of "Fragrant Rice" 307

— Performed by the Nanjing Mass Drama Society

The Stage of "Suicide" 308

— Performed by the Nanjing Popular Drama Society

Page 21

The barrenness of the theatrical world. However, comparatively speaking, there are a few minor controversies worth mentioning. The first is the different reviews caused by the performance of "Noble People". At that time, the criticisms of this play in various newspapers were said to be "more complimentary than strictly critical." Later, four gentlemen, including Li Ren, in "Performing Arts," and Mr. Sheng Fu in this publication, successively published two relatively strict criticisms, pointing out that the author could not completely "grasp objective reality and correctly portray it." Although this may seem a bit "harsh," the author, Ling He, has partially accepted this shortcoming, and he has partially corrected it in the standalone edition of the play.

Secondly, Mei Lanfang's trip to Russia has continued to attract considerable attention. Some people have said with extreme sarcasm and contempt that Dr. Mei's trip to Russia is to "go on a mission," while others regard the Russian invitation as a victory for the "Symbolist" Chinese opera and thus prove the decline of Soviet Russian realism. However, others say that these are all superficial and shallow views, arguing that the Soviet Russian invitation is to study the form and performance methods of Chinese opera, critically accepting the legacy of Eastern feudal art in order to build a new performing art. Regarding this issue, the China Daily News Drama Weekly published some insightful discussions in issues 10 through 16, which attracted great attention.

The issue of radio drama broadcasts also caused a minor controversy. In "Drama Weekly" and the Min Bao's "Drama Movement," several readers expressed disagreement with the current radio dramas, considering them to be nothing more than a "neighbor's play," a "modern storytelling," or a "new-style storytelling." The former even pointed out the emptiness and boredom of current radio dramas. Later, a gentleman in the Ta Wan Pao's Torch argued that radio drama has value, but this opinion did not attract much attention. Personally, I feel that radio drama has the possibility and necessity to become an independent art form, but I am also deeply dissatisfied with the boredom and chaos of the current radio drama broadcasting world.

The issue of popular language and drama also seemed to have caused a period of discussion. However, most opinions believe that if drama is to be popularized, the use of popular language is a necessary result, so there are no differing opinions.

(3) Performance Summary | Here, I want to describe some things about this year's performances. Let's start with Shanghai:

(1) Variety Shows | A Special Form of Performance in Shanghai: Shanghai's theater performers have a kind of distress, which is that they have plays but cannot perform them. This naturally has both subjective and objective reasons. Therefore, they have no choice but to accept invitations from social groups for variety shows. I think the following variety shows this year are more decent and worth mentioning:

The first was the performance of "Noble People," written and directed by film critic Ling He at the invitation of the Table Yearbook Association. This is not purely a variety show, but it is not purely a "public performance" either, so I still classify it as a variety show.

The second was the variety show of the Women's Voice Society. This time, a total of four plays were performed: "Oppression," "A Midsummer Night's Dream," "Miracle," and "Three Sisters." Except for "Oppression," the other three plays were mostly new works of this year. The performance effects were generally well-received by the newspapers.

The third was the variety show of the Mulun Middle School. This time, a total of four plays were performed: "The Peddler in the Snow," "Yangtze River Storm," "Nora After Leaving Home," and "Tight Report." "The Peddler in the Snow" did not perform well due to its inferior creative technique. "Tight Report" and "Nora After Leaving Home" were still able to satisfy the audience, but the best effect was achieved by "Yangtze River Storm." This is a new form of opera with substantial content, exquisite writing techniques, and excellent acting skills. This is probably the most successful work of 1934.

The fourth was the variety show of the Hunan Fellow Villagers Association. There was only one scene of spoken drama, "Extra," and the effect and content were acceptable.

(2) Public Performances | Although there were several public performances, they do not seem to have attracted much attention. At the end of May, the Fudan Drama Society performed "The Emperor Jones," which was criticized as a "child's play." The results can be imagined. In June, the Shang College Drama Society premiered "Father Returns" and "Relighting the Broken Fire." One drawback of this public performance was that these two plays were not easy to attract audiences. The Shanghai University National Drama Society performed "The Second Dream," which also committed the same mistake. The Jinan Drama Society also staged "Good May Not Be Willing," "Collecting Fishing Tax," and "Tide" at this time, which also did not attract much attention. Recently, the John Drama Society performed "Death of a Famous Actor," "Wangba," and "Executioner," and the Qingzhong Drama Society of the YMCA Middle School also performed "Fool" and "Great Thief," but both were limited to the small scope of the school and failed to attract a wide audience. In addition, the Shanghai University Drama Association staged four plays, "Maona Vanna," "Poor Pei Jia," "Self-Help," and "John Manley," on August 16th and 17th, which were able to attract some attention.

General social theater groups also lacked expression. The Drama Association has not had any expression since the public performance of "Roar, China." Several theater groups in 1933 have also disappeared. Although an unknown theater group staged several plays in the spring, such as "Laundry Boss and Poet," "Who is a Friend," "Locked Box," "Whaling," "Wanderer," "Plum Rain," "Brothers," and "Three Families Living Together," the scale was not large, but it had a small effect. Another Tuosheng Drama Society performed O'Neill's "Beyond the Horizon," which was considered an effort. The Lingling Drama Society performed several old plays such as "White Tea," "Consensus," "Way Out," and "Thief." The Ant Drama Troupe performed "Father Returns," "Moon Rising," and "Jinbao" in June, which were well-received. Some of these theater groups were just a flash in the pan, and some have not been heard from since (it is said that Ant is preparing for a performance). In addition, some spoken dramas are often performed in variety shows in major and minor schools and girls' schools, but some of these so-called spoken dramas have "famous" guest appearances, and some are just a riot, performing civilized plays. Here, I can only give a general overview and not mention them in detail.

In Nanjing, this year is "Drama Year," and public performances are often heard of. In the spring, Tang Huaiqiu's Chinese Touring Theater Troupe staged "Meiluo Xiang" in Nanjing, and the ticket price was sold for five yuan, and the business was good. Later, this theater troupe joined with nine groups, including the Chinese Literature and Art Society, the Contradiction Society, and the Popular Drama Society, to stage several old plays such as "Oppression," "Fool," "Woman and Dog," and "Gentleman on the Beam," but they did not attract much attention. In early May, the Popular Drama Society staged "Fragrant Rice," which caused a stir for a while. There were many criticisms in the newspapers, indicating that this play had a lot of appeal. The Chinese Drama Association staged Xiao Boner's "Heroes and Beauties" in June after performing plays such as "Fool." The content of this play was quite criticized, but the scenery was good. Soon, the Nandi Drama Society also performed "Salome." During the summer vacation, the Shanghai Dadi Drama Society went to Nanjing to stage plays such as "Death of a Famous Actor," "The Miser," "Father and Teacher," "Thief," and "Prison," which were able to attract some attention. In the autumn, the Youth Drama Society staged plays such as "Prison," "Thief," and "Selling Cattle," and the Popular Drama Society staged plays such as "Suicide" and "Three Sheng of Rice." The Xinyue Drama Society staged plays such as "Buying and Selling" and "The Last Embrace." All were small-scale.

In the north, Beiping has always been the place with the strongest drama atmosphere, but this year it is particularly deserted. The only public performance worth mentioning was "The Butcher," performed by the Beiping Drama Society organized by Xiong Fuxi and Zhang Mingqi in August. In addition, although the "Northern Country" and "Shacheng" drama societies had public performance plans, they both disappeared silently. Yu Shangyuan's small theater now only has an empty shell with a grand sign. Tang Huaiqiu's touring theater troupe brought to Beiping some old plays from seven or eight years ago and three or four years ago, such as "Meiluo Xiang," "The Female Shopkeeper," "Death of a Famous Actor," "Parasitic Grass," "Drunk," "White Tea," "Jealousy," "Buying and Selling," and "Fool." The theater scene in Beiping this year is really too barren. In Tianjin, the Parrot and Weimo drama societies have both performed plays this year, and the Gusong Drama Society has also performed "Drunk" and "Disabled," but these have not attracted people's attention.

In Guangzhou in the south, the spoken drama atmosphere was very prosperous during the "January 28th" commemoration. At that time, there were several plays such as the City Beauty Drama Society's "Two Wounded Soldiers," the Peizheng Literary Research Association's "Death of Shui Xinglin," the Zhongda Anti-Japanese Drama Society's "Comrades" and "Way Out," the Provincial First Vocational Drama Society's "Night Express," and the four schools' joint performance of "Order to Retreat to the Second Line of Defense," which were all good. In March, the Provincial First Vocational School also performed "Night Express" and "The Last Line." At that time, the Taishan Expedition Team was organized by the Yuanshu Middle School Drama Troupe to perform plays such as "Buying and Selling," "Behind the Screen," and "White Tea." After that, there were some unimportant sporadic public performances by some school drama societies. In August, the People's Education Center performed three plays, "Artist," "Sisters," and "Chastity." On September 18th, "Roar, China" was performed, but the lyrics were mostly revised. The People's Education Center opened a drama research institute in August, which now has more than 60 students.

In addition, there are unimportant sporadic performances in cities across the country such as Hangzhou, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Wuhu, Nanchang, Chongqing, Jinan, Xiamen, etc. Here, I will give a general overview and not mention them in detail.

(4) Rural Drama Movement | Xiong Fuxi in Dingxian and Gu Jianchen in Wuxi are both doing rural drama work to some extent. Mr. Xiong's purpose is to cultivate farmers' interest in drama and their automatic engagement in drama activities, in order to achieve the effect of civilian education. Mr. Xiong's efforts are commendable, but the things he gives to the farmers, such as "Trumpet," "Butcher," "Cow," and "Hoe Athletes," cannot alleviate the farmers' hunger. Although the public performance of "Trumpet" on Double Tenth Festival was "novel," it only affected a very small number of farmers. The commemorative public performance of the first farmer's open-air theater on the 2nd of this month included plays such as "Trumpet," "Drunkard," "Wang Si," "Moon Rising," "Dead End," "Lan Zhi and Zhong Qing," "Three Cows," "Marriage Proposal," "Fox Fairy Temple," and "Butcher," most of which lacked a close relationship with the real life of farmers. As for Mr. Gu, although he does have research on "costume speech," he is not as good as Mr. Xiong in other aspects.

(5) The So-Called Experimental Theater Society | Finally, I want to mention the Shandong Provincial Experimental Theater, which was recently established and is led by Wang Bosheng. Wang Bosheng used to be engaged in spoken drama, but later became a "famous amateur" and "famous actor." He even came to Shanghai this year to perform Beijing opera. Now he is appreciated by the Shandong art education community. He mainly engages in Beijing opera there. Although Zhang Mingqi and others cooperate in spoken drama, it is listed in an unimportant position.

This is all I have to say. The year 1934 has passed, and now we can only look forward to a richer harvest in 1935.

Ballad Singing 315

Yao Xiaoan Wang Pingqiu Pearl Tower

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "New Year's Day"

The New Year is a time of joy and peace. People are long-lived and the world is peaceful. The sound of firecrackers removes the old year. Peach charms renew spring in thousands of households. Children riding bamboo horses are a welcome sight. Grey-haired elders burn incense. Elegant disciples are busy dressing up. Graceful beauties. See those sesame stalks inserted high in front. See those pine and cypress trees with evergreen. Door gods have already been posted on the front door. There is also a spring couplet on both sides. The first line is that heaven bestows peace and happiness upon the family. The second line is that all the talented children in the world bring wealth and spring. The back door is posted with Zhong Jinshi. The other side is written Yichun. The poor live in bustling cities and no one asks. The rich live deep in the mountains and have distant relatives. The first day of spring is a time of movement. Renewing the four seeds brings a full spring. Thousands of households rejoice.

Guanyin Society

"Blood Flower"

Ms. Gan never dreamed that she would die at Ge Neng's hands. Although Ge Neng killed Ms. Gan, he himself also died. It's a pity that this group of revolutionary youths, holding the ideal of overthrowing warlords and fighting for freedom for the common people, were one by one sacrificed at the hands of the warlords.

"Happy Enemies"

What exactly is Bai Guiying's identity? The Yu Cheng couple spent several days racking their brains and finally found out. In a feudal village, a stage performer is never well-regarded, and Guiying is a woman, so naturally many people will spread this as news.

Li Shude (940) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

"Lonely Wild Duck at Sunset"

Feng Yuru was forced to meet Lu Boqing, just as she expected. Sure enough, Lu Boqing saw Yuru and refused to let her leave. In her anxiety, Yuru fell ill in the hotel. Lu Boqing brought a doctor to treat her. The doctor said, "This is caused by unhappiness and excessive worry. She should often go to a quiet mountain area for recuperation." Upon hearing this, Boqing sent Yuru to the Xishan Sanatorium.

Huamei (1060) 10:00 PM to 11:00 PM

"Man Jiang Hong"

The next morning, Li Taozhi went to the Gaosheng Hotel to meet Wan Youguang. As soon as she reached the door, she heard laughter inside. Listening carefully, it was Minister Yan's father, Yan Zhengxin, and Wan Youguang talking and laughing inside. The two of them were together looking at Yu Shuicun's work. Taozhi went in, and Yan Zhengxin said that Yu Shuicun's painting was really good and that he would promote Yu Shuicun. However, Taozhi could only say it in her heart and could not tell him his real name, so she went home unhappily.

News and Information 317

The Shanghai Guanyin Drama Society, which has a long history in the broadcasting world, will broadcast "Empty Valley Orchid" daily from January 1st of the 24th year, from 7:15 PM to 8:00 PM at Zhongxi Radio Station. Male actors include Mr. Chen Dabei, Mr. Gu Wenzong, and Mr. Xu Jingsheng. Female actors include Miss Jingya, Miss Xiong Li, and Miss Li Sai. The playwright is Mr. Bai Xiongfei. In addition to Mr. Bai himself, Mr. Liu Yiming will assist with the dubbing. This is also good news for the broadcasting world in the 214th year. The Fine Arts Training Lectures broadcast on Shanghai Radio Station will hold a meal meeting for members at the Da Zhonghua (Shilu) restaurant at noon in three weeks (30th). There will be various fine arts entertainment activities, and photos will be taken as a memento. People from all walks of life who love art are welcome to participate freely.
